<s> pg-viii PREFACE TO THE FOURTH EDITION </s>
<s> The chief alterations, since the First Edition, have been made in the Chapter on 'Classification' (pp </s>
<s> 2, 3) and the Book on 'Propositions' (pp </s>
<s> 10 to 19) </s>
<s> The chief additions have been the questions on words and phrases, added to the Examination-Papers at p </s>
<s> 94, and the Notes inserted at pp </s>
<s> 164, 194 </s>
<s> In Book I, Chapter II, I have adopted a new definition of 'Classification', which enables me to regard the whole Universe as a 'Class,' and thus to dispense with the very awkward phrase 'a Set of Things' </s>
<s> In the Chapter on 'Propositions of Existence' I have adopted a new 'normal form,' in which the Class, whose existence is affirmed or denied, is regarded as the _Predicate_, instead of the _Subject_, of the Proposition, thus evading a very subtle difficulty which besets the other form </s>
<s> These subtle difficulties seem to lie at the root of every Tree of Knowledge, and they are _far_ more hopeless to grapple with than any that occur in its higher branches </s>
<s> For example, the difficulties of the Forty-Seventh Proposition of Euclid are mere child's play compared with the mental torture endured in the effort to think out the essential nature of a straight Line </s>
<s> And, in the present work, the difficulties of the "5 Liars" Problem, at p </s>
<s> 192, are "trifles, light as air," compared with the bewildering question "What is a Thing" </s>
<s> In the Chapter on 'Propositions of Relation' I have inserted a new Section, containing the proof that a Proposition, beginning with "All," is a _Double_ Proposition (a fact that is quite independent of the arbitrary rule, laid down in the next Section, that such a Proposition is to be understood as implying the actual _existence_ of its Subject) </s>
<s> This proof was given, in the earlier editions, incidentally, in the course of the discussion of the Biliteral Diagram: but its _proper_ place, in this treatise, is where I have now introduced it </s>
<s> pg-ix In the Sorites-Examples, I have made a good many verbal alterations, in order to evade a difficulty, which I fear will have perplexed some of the Readers of the first three Editions </s>
<s> Some of the Premisses were so worded that their Terms were not Specieses of the Univ </s>
<s> named in the Dictionary, but of a larger Class, of which the Univ </s>
<s> was only a portion </s>
<s> In all such cases, it was intended that the Reader should perceive that what was asserted of the larger Class was thereby asserted of the Univ., and should ignore, as superfluous, all that it asserted of its _other_ portion </s>
<s> Thus, in Ex </s>
<s> 15, the Univ </s>
<s> was stated to be "ducks in this village," and the third Premiss was "Mrs Bond has no gray ducks," i.e </s>
<s> "No gray ducks are ducks belonging to Mrs Bond" </s>
<s> Here the Terms are _not_ Specieses of the Univ., but of the larger Class "ducks," of which the Univ </s>
<s> is only a portion: and it was intended that the Reader should perceive that what is here asserted of "ducks" is thereby asserted of "ducks in this village" </s>
<s> and should treat this Premiss as if it were "Mrs Bond has no gray ducks in this village," and should ignore, as superfluous, what it asserts as to the _other_ portion of the Class "ducks," viz </s>
<s> "Mrs Bond has no gray ducks _out of_ this village" </s>
<s> In the Appendix I have given a new version of the Problem of the "Five Liars" </s>
<s> My object, in doing so, is to escape the subtle and mysterious difficulties which beset all attempts at regarding a Proposition as being its own Subject, or a Set of Propositions as being Subjects for one another </s>
<s> It is certainly, a most bewildering and unsatisfactory theory: one cannot help feeling that there is a great lack of _substance_ in all this shadowy host----that, as the procession of phantoms glides before us, there is not _one_ that we can pounce upon, and say "_Here_ is a Proposition that _must_ be either true or false"!----that it is but a Barmecide Feast, to which we have been bidden----and that its prototype is to be found in that mythical island, whose inhabitants "earned a precarious living by taking in each others' washing" </s>
<s> By simply translating "telling 2 Truths" into "taking _both_ of 2 condiments (salt and mustard)," "telling 2 Lies" into "taking _neither_ of them" and "telling a Truth and a Lie (order not specified)" into "taking only _one_ condiment (it is not specified _which_)," I have escaped all those metaphysical puzzles, and have produced a Problem which, when translated into a Set of symbolized Premisses, furnishes the very same _Data_ as were furnished by the Problem of the "Five Liars" </s>
<s> pg-x The coined words, introduced in previous editions, such as "Eliminands" and "Retinends", perhaps hardly need any apology: they were indispensable to my system: but the new plural, here used for the first time, viz </s>
<s> "Soriteses", will, I fear, be condemned as "bad English", unless I say a word in its defence </s>
<s> We have _three_ singular nouns, in English, of plural _form_, "series", "species", and "Sorites": in all three, the awkwardness, of using the same word for both singular and plural, must often have been felt: this has been remedied, in the case of "series" by coining the plural "serieses", which has already found its way into the dictionaries: so I am no rash innovator, but am merely "following suit", in using the new plural "Soriteses" </s>
<s> In conclusion, let me point out that even those, who are obliged to study _Formal_ Logic, with a view to being able to answer Examination-Papers in that subject, will find the study of _Symbolic_ Logic most helpful for this purpose, in throwing light upon many of the obscurities with which Formal Logic abounds, and in furnishing a delightfully easy method of _testing_ the results arrived at by the cumbrous processes which Formal Logic enforces upon its votaries </s>
<s> This is, I believe, the very first attempt (with the exception of my own little book, _The Game of Logic_, published in 1886, a very incomplete performance) that has been made to _popularise_ this fascinating subject </s>
<s> It has cost me _years_ of hard work: but if it should prove, as I hope it may, to be of _real_ service to the young, and to be taken up, in High Schools and in private families, as a valuable addition to their stock of healthful mental recreations, such a result would more than repay ten times the labour that I have expended on it </s>
<s> L </s>
<s> C </s>
<s> 29, BEDFORD STREET, STRAND </s>
<s> _Christmas, 1896._ pg-xi INTRODUCTION </s>
<s> _TO LEARNERS._ [N.B </s>
<s> Some remarks, addressed to _Teachers_, will be found in the Appendix, at p </s>
<s> 165.] The Learner, who wishes to try the question _fairly_, whether this little book does, or does not, supply the materials for a most interesting mental recreation, is _earnestly_ advised to adopt the following Rules:-- (1) Begin at the _beginning_, and do not allow yourself to gratify a mere idle curiosity by dipping into the book, here and there </s>
<s> This would very likely lead to your throwing it aside, with the remark "This is _much_ too hard for me"!, and thus losing the chance of adding a very _large_ item to your stock of mental delights </s>
<s> This Rule (of not _dipping_) is very _desirable_ with _other_ kinds of books----such as novels, for instance, where you may easily spoil much of the enjoyment you would otherwise get from the story, by dipping into it further on, so that what the author meant to be a pleasant surprise comes to you as a matter of course </s>
<s> Some people, I know, make a practice of looking into Vol </s>
<s> III first, just to see how the story ends: and perhaps it _is_ as well just to know that all ends _happily_----that the much-persecuted lovers _do_ marry after all, that he is proved to be quite innocent of the murder, that the wicked cousin is completely foiled in his plot and gets the punishment he deserves, and that the rich uncle in India (_Qu._ Why in _India_ </s>
<s> _Ans._ Because, somehow, uncles never _can_ get rich anywhere else) dies at exactly the right moment----before taking the trouble to read Vol </s>
<s> I </s>
<s> This, I say, is _just_ permissible with a _novel_, where Vol </s>
<s> III has a _meaning_, even for those who have not read the earlier part of the story; but, with a _scientific_ book, it is sheer insanity: you will find the latter part _hopelessly_ unintelligible, if you read it before reaching it in regular course </s>
<s> pg-xii (2) Don't begin any fresh Chapter, or Section, until you are certain that you _thoroughly_ understand the whole book _up to that point_, and that you have worked, correctly, most if not all of the examples which have been set </s>
<s> So long as you are conscious that all the land you have passed through is absolutely _conquered_, and that you are leaving no unsolved difficulties _behind_ you, which will be sure to turn up again later on, your triumphal progress will be easy and delightful </s>
<s> Otherwise, you will find your state of puzzlement get worse and worse as you proceed, till you give up the whole thing in utter disgust </s>
<s> (3) When you come to any passage you don't understand, _read it again_: if you _still_ don't understand it, _read it again_: if you fail, even after _three_ readings, very likely your brain is getting a little tired </s>
<s> In that case, put the book away, and take to other occupations, and next day, when you come to it fresh, you will very likely find that it is _quite_ easy </s>
<s> (4) If possible, find some genial friend, who will read the book along with you, and will talk over the difficulties with you </s>
<s> _Talking_ is a wonderful smoother-over of difficulties </s>
<s> When _I_ come upon anything----in Logic or in any other hard subject----that entirely puzzles me, I find it a capital plan to talk it over, _aloud_, even when I am all alone </s>
<s> One can explain things so _clearly_ to one's self </s>
<s> And then, you know, one is so _patient_ with one's self: one _never_ gets irritated at one's own stupidity </s>
<s> If, dear Reader, you will faithfully observe these Rules, and so give my little book a really _fair_ trial, I promise you, most confidently, that you will find Symbolic Logic to be one of the most, if not _the_ most, fascinating of mental recreations </s>
<s> In this First Part, I have carefully avoided all difficulties which seemed to me to be beyond the grasp of an intelligent child of (say) twelve or fourteen years of age </s>
<s> I have myself taught most of its contents, _vivÃ¢ voce_, to _many_ children, and have found them take a real intelligent interest in the subject </s>
<s> For those, who succeed in mastering Part I, and who begin, like Oliver, "asking for more," I hope to provide, in Part II, some _tolerably_ hard nuts to crack----nuts that will require all the nut-crackers they happen to possess </s>
<s> pg-xiii Mental recreation is a thing that we all of us need for our mental health; and you may get much healthy enjoyment, no doubt, from Games, such as Back-gammon, Chess, and the new Game "Halma" </s>
<s> But, after all, when you have made yourself a first-rate player at any one of these Games, you have nothing real to _show_ for it, as a _result!_ You enjoyed the Game, and the victory, no doubt, _at the time_: but you have no _result_ that you can treasure up and get real _good_ out of </s>
<s> And, all the while, you have been leaving unexplored a perfect _mine_ of wealth </s>
<s> Once master the machinery of Symbolic Logic, and you have a mental occupation always at hand, of absorbing interest, and one that will be of real _use_ to you in _any_ subject you may take up </s>
<s> It will give you clearness of thought----the ability to _see your way_ through a puzzle----the habit of arranging your ideas in an orderly and get-at-able form----and, more valuable than all, the power to detect _fallacies_, and to tear to pieces the flimsy illogical arguments, which you will so continually encounter in books, in newspapers, in speeches, and even in sermons, and which so easily delude those who have never taken the trouble to master this fascinating Art </s>
<s> _Try it._ That is all I ask of you </s>
<s> L </s>
<s> C </s>

<s> explained " pg-xxxii pg001 BOOK I </s>
<s> THINGS AND THEIR ATTRIBUTES </s>
<s> CHAPTER I </s>
<s> _INTRODUCTORY._ The Universe contains '=Things=' </s>
<s> [For example, "I," "London," "roses," "redness," "old English books," "the letter which I received yesterday".] Things have '=Attributes=' </s>
<s> [For example, "large," "red," "old," "which I received yesterday".] One Thing may have many Attributes; and one Attribute may belong to many Things </s>
<s> [Thus, the Thing "a rose" may have the Attributes "red," "scented," "full-blown," &c.; and the Attribute "red" may belong to the Things "a rose," "a brick," "a ribbon," &c.] Any Attribute, or any Set of Attributes, may be called an '=Adjunct=' </s>
<s> [This word is introduced in order to avoid the constant repetition of the phrase "Attribute or Set of Attributes" </s>
<s> Thus, we may say that a rose has the Attribute "red" (or the Adjunct "red," whichever we prefer); or we may say that it has the Adjunct "red, scented and full-blown".] pg001Â½ CHAPTER II </s>
<s> _CLASSIFICATION._ 'Classification,' or the formation of Classes, is a Mental Process, in which we imagine that we have put together, in a group, certain Things </s>
<s> Such a group is called a '=Class=' </s>
<s> This Process may be performed in three different ways, as follows:-- (1) We may imagine that we have put together all Things </s>
<s> The Class so formed (i.e </s>
<s> the Class "Things") contains the whole Universe </s>
<s> (2) We may think of the Class "Things," and may imagine that we have picked out from it all the Things which possess a certain Adjunct _not_ possessed by the whole Class </s>
<s> This Adjunct is said to be '=peculiar=' to the Class so formed </s>
<s> In this case, the Class "Things" is called a '=Genus=' with regard to the Class so formed: the Class, so formed, is called a '=Species=' of the Class "Things": and its peculiar Adjunct is called its '=Differentia=' </s>
<s> pg002 As this Process is entirely _Mental_, we can perform it whether there _is_, or _is not_, an _existing_ Thing which possesses that Adjunct </s>
<s> If there _is_, the Class is said to be '=Real='; if not, it is said to be '=Unreal=', or '=Imaginary=' </s>
<s> [For example, we may imagine that we have picked out, from the Class "Things," all the Things which possess the Adjunct "material, artificial, consisting of houses and streets"; and we may thus form the Real Class "towns" </s>
<s> Here we may regard "Things" as a _Genus_, "Towns" as a _Species_ of Things, and "material, artificial, consisting of houses and streets" as its _Differentia_ </s>
<s> Again, we may imagine that we have picked out all the Things which possess the Adjunct "weighing a ton, easily lifted by a baby"; and we may thus form the _Imaginary_ Class "Things that weigh a ton and are easily lifted by a baby".] (3) We may think of a certain Class, _not_ the Class "Things," and may imagine that we have picked out from it all the Members of it which possess a certain Adjunct _not_ possessed by the whole Class </s>
<s> This Adjunct is said to be '=peculiar=' to the smaller Class so formed </s>
<s> In this case, the Class thought of is called a '=Genus=' with regard to the smaller Class picked out from it: the smaller Class is called a '=Species=' of the larger: and its peculiar Adjunct is called its '=Differentia=' </s>
<s> [For example, we may think of the Class "towns," and imagine that we have picked out from it all the towns which possess the Attribute "lit with gas"; and we may thus form the Real Class "towns lit with gas" </s>
<s> Here we may regard "Towns" as a _Genus_, "Towns lit with gas" as a _Species_ of Towns, and "lit with gas" as its _Differentia_ </s>
<s> If, in the above example, we were to alter "lit with gas" into "paved with gold," we should get the _Imaginary_ Class "towns paved with gold".] A Class, containing only _one_ Member is called an '=Individual=' </s>
<s> [For example, the Class "towns having four million inhabitants," which Class contains only _one_ Member, viz </s>
<s> "London".] pg002Â½ Hence, any single Thing, which we can name so as to distinguish it from all other Things, may be regarded as a one-Member Class </s>
<s> [Thus "London" may be regarded as the one-Member Class, picked out from the Class "towns," which has, as its Differentia, "having four million inhabitants".] A Class, containing two or more Members, is sometimes regarded as _one single Thing_ </s>
<s> When so regarded, it may possess an Adjunct which is _not_ possessed by any Member of it taken separately </s>
<s> [Thus, the Class "The soldiers of the Tenth Regiment," when regarded as _one single Thing_, may possess the Attribute "formed in square," which is _not_ possessed by any Member of it taken separately.] pg003 CHAPTER III </s>
<s> _DIVISION._ Â§ 1 </s>
<s> _Introductory._ 'Division' is a Mental Process, in which we think of a certain Class of Things, and imagine that we have divided it into two or more smaller Classes </s>
<s> [Thus, we might think of the Class "books," and imagine that we had divided it into the two smaller Classes "bound books" and "unbound books," or into the three Classes, "books priced at less than a shilling," "shilling-books," "books priced at more than a shilling," or into the twenty-six Classes, "books whose names begin with _A_," "books whose names begin with _B_," &c.] A Class, that has been obtained by a certain Division, is said to be 'codivisional' with every Class obtained by that Division </s>
<s> [Thus, the Class "bound books" is codivisional with each of the two Classes, "bound books" and "unbound books" </s>
<s> Similarly, the Battle of Waterloo may be said to have been "contemporary" with every event that happened in 1815.] Hence a Class, obtained by Division, is codivisional with itself </s>
<s> [Thus, the Class "bound books" is codivisional with itself </s>
<s> Similarly, the Battle of Waterloo may be said to have been "contemporary" with itself.] pg003Â½ Â§ 2 </s>
<s> _Dichotomy._ If we think of a certain Class, and imagine that we have picked out from it a certain smaller Class, it is evident that the _Remainder_ of the large Class does _not_ possess the Differentia of that smaller Class </s>
<s> Hence it may be regarded as _another_ smaller Class, whose Differentia may be formed, from that of the Class first picked out, by prefixing the word "not"; and we may imagine that we have _divided_ the Class first thought of into _two_ smaller Classes, whose DifferentiÃ¦ are _contradictory_ </s>
<s> This kind of Division is called '=Dichotomy=' </s>
<s> [For example, we may divide "books" into the two Classes whose DifferentiÃ¦ are "old" and "not-old".] In performing this Process, we may sometimes find that the Attributes we have chosen are used so loosely, in ordinary conversation, that it is not easy to decide _which_ of the Things belong to the one Class and _which_ to the other </s>
<s> In such a case, it would be necessary to lay down some arbitrary _rule_, as to _where_ the one Class should end and the other begin </s>
<s> [Thus, in dividing "books" into "old" and "not-old," we may say "Let all books printed before A.D </s>
<s> 1801, be regarded as 'old,' and all others as 'not-old'".] Henceforwards let it be understood that, if a Class of Things be divided into two Classes, whose DifferentiÃ¦ have contrary meanings, each Differentia is to be regarded as equivalent to the other with the word "not" prefixed </s>
<s> [Thus, if "books" be divided into "old" and "new" the Attribute "old" is to be regarded as equivalent to "not-new," and the Attribute "new" as equivalent to "not-old".] pg004 After dividing a Class, by the Process of _Dichotomy_, into two smaller Classes, we may sub-divide each of these into two still smaller Classes; and this Process may be repeated over and over again, the number of Classes being doubled at each repetition </s>
<s> [For example, we may divide "books" into "old" and "new" (i.e </s>
<s> "_not_-old"): we may then sub-divide each of these into "English" and "foreign" (i.e </s>
<s> "_not_-English"), thus getting _four_ Classes, viz </s>
<s> (1) old English; (2) old foreign; (3) new English; (4) new foreign </s>
<s> If we had begun by dividing into "English" and "foreign," and had then sub-divided into "old" and "new," the four Classes would have been (1) English old; (2) English new; (3) foreign old; (4) foreign new </s>
<s> The Reader will easily see that these are the very same four Classes which we had before.] pg004Â½ CHAPTER IV </s>
<s> _NAMES._ The word "Thing", which conveys the idea of a Thing, _without_ any idea of an Adjunct, represents _any_ single Thing </s>
<s> Any other word (or phrase), which conveys the idea of a Thing, _with_ the idea of an Adjunct represents _any_ Thing which possesses that Adjunct; i.e., it represents any Member of the Class to which that Adjunct is _peculiar_ </s>
<s> Such a word (or phrase) is called a '=Name='; and, if there be an existing Thing which it represents, it is said to be a Name of that Thing </s>
<s> [For example, the words "Thing," "Treasure," "Town," and the phrases "valuable Thing," "material artificial Thing consisting of houses and streets," "Town lit with gas," "Town paved with gold," "old English Book".] Just as a Class is said to be _Real_, or _Unreal_, according as there _is_, or _is not_, an existing Thing in it, so also a Name is said to be _Real_, or _Unreal_, according as there _is_, or _is not_, an existing Thing represented by it </s>
<s> [Thus, "Town lit with gas" is a _Real_ Name: "Town paved with gold" is an _Unreal_ Name.] Every Name is either a Substantive only, or else a phrase consisting of a Substantive and one or more Adjectives (or phrases used as Adjectives) </s>
<s> Every Name, except "Thing", may usually be expressed in three different forms:-- (_a_) The Substantive "Thing", and one or more Adjectives (or phrases used as Adjectives) conveying the ideas of the Attributes; pg005 (_b_) A Substantive, conveying the idea of a Thing with the ideas of _some_ of the Attributes, and one or more Adjectives (or phrases used as Adjectives) conveying the ideas of the _other_ Attributes; (_c_) A Substantive conveying the idea of a Thing with the ideas of _all_ the Attributes </s>
<s> [Thus, the phrase "material living Thing, belonging to the Animal Kingdom, having two hands and two feet" is a Name expressed in Form (_a_) </s>
<s> If we choose to roll up together the Substantive "Thing" and the Adjectives "material, living, belonging to the Animal Kingdom," so as to make the new Substantive "Animal," we get the phrase "Animal having two hands and two feet," which is a Name (representing the same Thing as before) expressed in Form (_b_) </s>
<s> And, if we choose to roll up the whole phrase into one word, so as to make the new Substantive "Man," we get a Name (still representing the very same Thing) expressed in Form (_c_).] A Name, whose Substantive is in the _plural_ number, may be used to represent either (1) Members of a Class, _regarded as separate Things_; or (2) a whole Class, _regarded as one single Thing_ </s>
<s> [Thus, when I say "Some soldiers of the Tenth Regiment are tall," or "The soldiers of the Tenth Regiment are brave," I am using the Name "soldiers of the Tenth Regiment" in the _first_ sense; and it is just the same as if I were to point to each of them _separately_, and to say "_This_ soldier of the Tenth Regiment is tall," "_That_ soldier of the Tenth Regiment is tall," and so on </s>
<s> But, when I say "The soldiers of the Tenth Regiment are formed in square," I am using the phrase in the _second_ sense; and it is just the same as if I were to say "The _Tenth Regiment_ is formed in square".] pg006 CHAPTER V </s>
<s> _DEFINITIONS._ It is evident that every Member of a _Species_ is _also_ a Member of the _Genus_ out of which that Species has been picked, and that it possesses the _Differentia_ of that Species </s>
<s> Hence it may be represented by a Name consisting of two parts, one being a Name representing any Member of the _Genus_, and the other being the _Differentia_ of that Species </s>
<s> Such a Name is called a '=Definition=' of any Member of that Species, and to give it such a Name is to '=define=' it </s>
<s> [Thus, we may define a "Treasure" as a "valuable Thing" </s>
<s> In this case we regard "Things" as the _Genus_, and "valuable" as the _Differentia_.] The following Examples, of this Process, may be taken as models for working others </s>
<s> [Note that, in each Definition, the Substantive, representing a Member (or Members) of the _Genus_, is printed in Capitals.] 1 </s>
<s> Define "a Treasure" </s>
<s> _Ans._ "a valuable THING" </s>
<s> 2 </s>
<s> Define "Treasures" </s>
<s> _Ans._ "valuable THINGS" </s>
<s> 3 </s>
<s> Define "a Town" </s>
<s> _Ans._ "a material artificial THING, consisting of houses and streets" </s>
<s> pg007 4 </s>
<s> Define "Men" </s>
<s> _Ans._ "material, living THINGS, belonging to the Animal Kingdom, having two hands and two feet"; or else "ANIMALS having two hands and two feet" </s>
<s> 5 </s>
<s> Define "London" </s>
<s> _Ans._ "the material artificial THING, which consists of houses and streets, and has four million inhabitants"; or else "the TOWN which has four million inhabitants" </s>
<s> [Note that we here use the article "the" instead of "a", because we happen to know that there is only _one_ such Thing </s>
<s> The Reader can set himself any number of Examples of this Process, by simply choosing the Name of any common Thing (such as "house," "tree," "knife"), making a Definition for it, and then testing his answer by referring to any English Dictionary.] pg008 BOOK II </s>
<s> PROPOSITIONS </s>
<s> CHAPTER I </s>
<s> _PROPOSITIONS GENERALLY._ Â§ 1 </s>
<s> _Introductory._ Note that the word "some" is to be regarded, henceforward, as meaning "one or more" </s>
<s> The word 'Proposition,' as used in ordinary conversation, may be applied to _any_ word, or phrase, which conveys any information whatever </s>
<s> [Thus the words "yes" and "no" are Propositions in the ordinary sense of the word; and so are the phrases "you owe me five farthings" and "I don't" </s>
<s> Such words as "oh" </s>
<s> or "never"!, and such phrases as "fetch me that book" </s>
<s> "which book do you mean" </s>
<s> do not seem, at first sight, to convey any _information_; but they can easily be turned into equivalent forms which do so, viz </s>
<s> "I am surprised," "I will never consent to it," "I order you to fetch me that book," "I want to know which book you mean".] But a '=Proposition=,' as used in this First Part of "Symbolic Logic," has a peculiar form, which may be called its '=Normal form='; and if any Proposition, which we wish to use in an argument, is not in normal form, we must reduce it to such a form, before we can use it </s>
<s> pg009 A '=Proposition=,' when in normal form, asserts, as to certain two Classes, which are called its '=Subject=' and '=Predicate=,' either (1) that _some_ Members of its Subject are Members of its Predicate; or (2) that _no_ Members of its Subject are Members of its Predicate; or (3) that _all_ Members of its Subject are Members of its Predicate </s>
<s> The Subject and the Predicate of a Proposition are called its '=Terms=' </s>
<s> Two Propositions, which convey the _same_ information, are said to be '=equivalent=' </s>
<s> [Thus, the two Propositions, "I see John" and "John is seen by me," are equivalent.] Â§ 2 </s>
<s> _Normal form of a Proposition._ A Proposition, in normal form, consists of four parts, viz.-- (1) The word "some," or "no," or "all" </s>
<s> (This word, which tells us _how many_ Members of the Subject are also Members of the Predicate, is called the '=Sign of Quantity='.) (2) Name of Subject </s>
<s> (3) The verb "are" (or "is") </s>
<s> (This is called the '=Copula='.) (4) Name of Predicate </s>
<s> pg010 Â§ 3 </s>
<s> _Various kinds of Propositions._ A Proposition, that begins with "Some", is said to be '=Particular=' </s>
<s> It is also called 'a Proposition =in I=' </s>
<s> [Note, that it is called 'Particular,' because it refers to a _part_ only of the Subject.] A Proposition, that begins with "No", is said to be '=Universal Negative=' </s>
<s> It is also called 'a Proposition =in E=' </s>
<s> A Proposition, that begins with "All", is said to be '=Universal Affirmative=' </s>
<s> It is also called 'a Proposition =in A=' </s>
<s> [Note, that they are called 'Universal', because they refer to the _whole_ of the Subject.] A Proposition, whose Subject is an _Individual_, is to be regarded as _Universal_ </s>
<s> [Let us take, as an example, the Proposition "John is not well" </s>
<s> This of course implies that there is an _Individual_, to whom the speaker refers when he mentions "John", and whom the listener _knows_ to be referred to </s>
<s> Hence the Class "men referred to by the speaker when he mentions 'John'" is a one-Member Class, and the Proposition is equivalent to "_All_ the men, who are referred to by the speaker when he mentions 'John', are not well".] Propositions are of two kinds, 'Propositions of Existence' and 'Propositions of Relation' </s>
<s> These shall be discussed separately </s>
<s> pg011 CHAPTER II </s>
<s> _PROPOSITIONS OF EXISTENCE._ A '=Proposition of Existence=', when in normal form, has, for its _Subject_, the Class "existing Things" </s>
<s> Its Sign of Quantity is "Some" or "No" </s>
<s> [Note that, though its Sign of Quantity tells us _how many_ existing Things are Members of its Predicate, it does _not_ tell us the _exact_ number: in fact, it only deals with _two_ numbers, which are, in ascending order, "0" and "1 or more".] It is called "a Proposition of Existence" because its effect is to assert the _Reality_ (i.e </s>
<s> the real _existence_), or else the _Imaginariness_, of its Predicate </s>
<s> [Thus, the Proposition "Some existing Things are honest men" asserts that the Class "honest men" is _Real_ </s>
<s> This is the _normal_ form; but it may also be expressed in any one of the following forms:-- (1) "Honest men exist"; (2) "Some honest men exist"; (3) "The Class 'honest men' exists"; (4) "There are honest men"; (5) "There are some honest men" </s>
<s> Similarly, the Proposition "No existing Things are men fifty feet high" asserts that the Class "men 50 feet high" is _Imaginary_ </s>
<s> This is the _normal_ form; but it may also be expressed in any one of the following forms:-- (1) "Men 50 feet high do not exist"; (2) "No men 50 feet high exist"; (3) "The Class 'men 50 feet high' does not exist"; (4) "There are not any men 50 feet high"; (5) "There are no men 50 feet high".] pg012 CHAPTER III </s>
<s> _PROPOSITIONS OF RELATION._ Â§ 1 </s>
<s> _Introductory._ A =Proposition of Relation=, of the kind to be here discussed, has, for its Terms, two Specieses of the same Genus, such that each of the two Names conveys the idea of some Attribute _not_ conveyed by the other </s>
<s> [Thus, the Proposition "Some merchants are misers" is of the right kind, since "merchants" and "misers" are Specieses of the same Genus "men"; and since the Name "merchants" conveys the idea of the Attribute "mercantile", and the name "misers" the idea of the Attribute "miserly", each of which ideas is _not_ conveyed by the other Name </s>
<s> But the Proposition "Some dogs are setters" is _not_ of the right kind, since, although it is true that "dogs" and "setters" are Specieses of the same Genus "animals", it is _not_ true that the Name "dogs" conveys the idea of any Attribute not conveyed by the Name "setters" </s>
<s> Such Propositions will be discussed in Part II.] The Genus, of which the two Terms are Specieses, is called the '=Universe of Discourse=,' or (more briefly) the '=Univ.=' The Sign of Quantity is "Some" or "No" or "All" </s>
<s> [Note that, though its Sign of Quantity tells us _how many_ Members of its Subject are _also_ Members of its Predicate, it does not tell us the _exact_ number: in fact, it only deals with _three_ numbers, which are, in ascending order, "0", "1 or more", "the total number of Members of the Subject".] It is called "a Proposition of Relation" because its effect is to assert that a certain _relationship_ exists between its Terms </s>
<s> pg013 Â§ 2 </s>
<s> _Reduction of a Proposition of Relation to Normal form._ The Rules, for doing this, are as follows:-- (1) Ascertain what is the _Subject_ (i.e., ascertain what Class we are _talking about_); (2) If the verb, governed by the Subject, is _not_ the verb "are" (or "is"), substitute for it a phrase beginning with "are" (or "is"); (3) Ascertain what is the _Predicate_ (i.e., ascertain what Class it is, which is asserted to contain _some_, or _none_, or _all_, of the Members of the Subject); (4) If the Name of each Term is _completely expressed_ (i.e </s>
<s> if it contains a Substantive), there is no need to determine the 'Univ'.; but, if either Name is _incompletely expressed_, and contains _Attributes_ only, it is then necessary to determine a 'Univ'., in order to insert its Name as the Substantive </s>
<s> (5) Ascertain the _Sign of Quantity_; (6) Arrange in the following order:-- Sign of Quantity, Subject, Copula, Predicate </s>
<s> [Let us work a few Examples, to illustrate these Rules </s>
<s> (1) "Some apples are not ripe" </s>
<s> (1) The Subject is "apples" </s>
<s> (2) The Verb is "are" </s>
<s> (3) The Predicate is "not-ripe * * *" </s>
<s> (As no Substantive is expressed, and we have not yet settled what the Univ </s>
<s> is to be, we are forced to leave a blank.) (4) Let Univ </s>
<s> be "fruit" </s>
<s> (5) The Sign of Quantity is "some" </s>
<s> (6) The Proposition now becomes "Some | apples | are | not-ripe fruit" </s>
<s> pg014 (2) "None of my speculations have brought me as much as 5 per cent" </s>
<s> (1) The Subject is "my speculations" </s>
<s> (2) The Verb is "have brought," for which we substitute the phrase "are * * * that have brought" </s>
<s> (3) The Predicate is "* * * that have brought &c" </s>
<s> (4) Let Univ </s>
<s> be "transactions" </s>
<s> (5) The Sign of Quantity is "none of" </s>
<s> (6) The Proposition now becomes "None of | my speculations | are | transactions that have brought me as much as 5 per cent" </s>
<s> (3) "None but the brave deserve the fair" </s>
<s> To begin with, we note that the phrase "none but the brave" is equivalent to "no _not_-brave" </s>
<s> (1) The Subject has for its _Attribute_ "not-brave" </s>
<s> But no _Substantive_ is supplied </s>
<s> So we express the Subject as "not-brave * * *" </s>
<s> (2) The Verb is "deserve," for which we substitute the phrase "are deserving of" </s>
<s> (3) The Predicate is "* * * deserving of the fair" </s>
<s> (4) Let Univ </s>
<s> be "persons" </s>
<s> (5) The Sign of Quantity is "no" </s>
<s> (6) The Proposition now becomes "No | not-brave persons | are | persons deserving of the fair" </s>
<s> (4) "A lame puppy would not say "thank you" if you offered to lend it a skipping-rope" </s>
<s> (1) The Subject is evidently "lame puppies," and all the rest of the sentence must somehow be packed into the Predicate </s>
<s> (2) The Verb is "would not say," &c., for which we may substitute the phrase "are not grateful for" </s>
<s> (3) The Predicate may be expressed as "* * * not grateful for the loan of a skipping-rope" </s>
<s> (4) Let Univ </s>
<s> be "puppies" </s>
<s> (5) The Sign of Quantity is "all" </s>
<s> (6) The Proposition now becomes "All | lame puppies | are | puppies not grateful for the loan of a skipping-rope" </s>
<s> pg015 (5) "No one takes in the _Times_, unless he is well-educated" </s>
<s> (1) The Subject is evidently persons who are not well-educated ("no _one_" evidently means "no _person_") </s>
<s> (2) The Verb is "takes in," for which we may substitute the phrase "are persons taking in" </s>
<s> (3) The Predicate is "persons taking in the _Times_" </s>
<s> (4) Let Univ </s>
<s> be "persons" </s>
<s> (5) The Sign of Quantity is "no" </s>
<s> (6) The Proposition now becomes "No | persons who are not well-educated | are | persons taking in the _Times_" </s>
<s> (6) "My carriage will meet you at the station" </s>
<s> (1) The Subject is "my carriage" </s>
<s> This, being an 'Individual,' is equivalent to the Class "my carriages" </s>
<s> (Note that this Class contains only _one_ Member.) (2) The Verb is "will meet", for which we may substitute the phrase "are * * * that will meet" </s>
<s> (3) The Predicate is "* * * that will meet you at the station" </s>
<s> (4) Let Univ </s>
<s> be "things" </s>
<s> (5) The Sign of Quantity is "all" </s>
<s> (6) The Proposition now becomes "All | my carriages | are | things that will meet you at the station" </s>
<s> (7) "Happy is the man who does not know what 'toothache' means" </s>
<s> (1) The Subject is evidently "the man &c" </s>
<s> (Note that in this sentence, the _Predicate_ comes first.) At first sight, the Subject seems to be an '_Individual_'; but on further consideration, we see that the article "the" does _not_ imply that there is only _one_ such man </s>
<s> Hence the phrase "the man who" is equivalent to "all men who" </s>
<s> (2) The Verb is "are" </s>
<s> (3) The Predicate is "happy * * *" </s>
<s> (4) Let Univ </s>
<s> be "men" </s>
<s> (5) The Sign of Quantity is "all" </s>
<s> (6) The Proposition now becomes "All | men who do not know what 'toothache' means | are | happy men" </s>
<s> pg016 (8) "Some farmers always grumble at the weather, whatever it may be" </s>
<s> (1) The Subject is "farmers" </s>
<s> (2) The Verb is "grumble," for which we substitute the phrase "are * * * who grumble" </s>
<s> (3) The Predicate is "* * * who always grumble &c" </s>
<s> (4) Let Univ </s>
<s> be "persons" </s>
<s> (5) The Sign of Quantity is "some" </s>
<s> (6) The Proposition now becomes "Some | farmers | are | persons who always grumble at the weather, whatever it may be" </s>
<s> (9) "No lambs are accustomed to smoke cigars" </s>
<s> (1) The Subject is "lambs" </s>
<s> (2) The Verb is "are" </s>
<s> (3) The Predicate is "* * * accustomed &c" </s>
<s> (4) Let Univ </s>
<s> be "animals" </s>
<s> (5) The Sign of Quantity is "no" </s>
<s> (6) The Proposition now becomes "No | lambs | are | animals accustomed to smoke cigars" </s>
<s> (10) "I ca'n't understand examples that are not arranged in regular order, like those I am used to" </s>
<s> (1) The Subject is "examples that," &c </s>
<s> (2) The Verb is "I ca'n't understand," which we must alter, so as to have "examples," instead of "I," as the nominative case </s>
<s> It may be expressed as "are not understood by me" </s>
<s> (3) The Predicate is "* * * not understood by me" </s>
<s> (4) Let Univ </s>
<s> be "examples" </s>
<s> (5) The Sign of Quantity is "all" </s>
<s> (6) The Proposition now becomes "All | examples that are not arranged in regular order like those I am used to | are | examples not understood by me".] pg017 Â§ 3 </s>
<s> _A Proposition of Relation, beginning with "All", is a Double Proposition._ A Proposition of Relation, beginning with "All", asserts (as we already know) that "_All_ Members of the Subject are Members of the Predicate" </s>
<s> This evidently contains, as a _part_ of what it tells us, the smaller Proposition "_Some_ Members of the Subject are Members of the Predicate" </s>
<s> [Thus, the Proposition "_All_ bankers are rich men" evidently contains the smaller Proposition "_Some_ bankers are rich men".] The question now arises "What is the _rest_ of the information which this Proposition gives us" </s>
<s> In order to answer this question, let us begin with the smaller Proposition, "_Some_ Members of the Subject are Members of the Predicate," and suppose that this is _all_ we have been told; and let us proceed to inquire what _else_ we need to be told, in order to know that "_All_ Members of the Subject are Members of the Predicate" </s>
<s> [Thus, we may suppose that the Proposition "_Some_ bankers are rich men" is all the information we possess; and we may proceed to inquire what _other_ Proposition needs to be added to it, in order to make up the entire Proposition "_All_ bankers are rich men".] Let us also suppose that the 'Univ' </s>
<s> (i.e </s>
<s> the Genus, of which both the Subject and the Predicate are Specieses) has been divided (by the Process of _Dichotomy_) into two smaller Classes, viz </s>
<s> (1) the Predicate; (2) the Class whose Differentia is _contradictory_ to that of the Predicate </s>
<s> [Thus, we may suppose that the Genus "men," (of which both "bankers" and "rich men" are Specieses) has been divided into the two smaller Classes, "rich men", "poor men".] pg018 Now we know that _every_ Member of the Subject is (as shown at p </s>
<s> 6) a Member of the Univ </s>
<s> Hence _every_ Member of the Subject is either in Class (1) or else in Class (2) </s>
<s> [Thus, we know that _every_ banker is a Member of the Genus "men" </s>
<s> Hence, _every_ banker is either in the Class "rich men", or else in the Class "poor men".] Also we have been told that, in the case we are discussing, _some_ Members of the Subject are in Class (1) </s>
<s> What _else_ do we need to be told, in order to know that _all_ of them are there </s>
<s> Evidently we need to be told that _none_ of them are in Class (2); i.e </s>
<s> that _none_ of them are Members of the Class whose Differentia is _contradictory_ to that of the Predicate </s>
<s> [Thus, we may suppose we have been told that _some_ bankers are in the Class "rich men" </s>
<s> What _else_ do we need to be told, in order to know that _all_ of them are there </s>
<s> Evidently we need to be told that _none_ of them are in the Class "_poor_ men".] Hence a Proposition of Relation, beginning with "All", is a _Double_ Proposition, and is '=equivalent=' to (i.e </s>
<s> gives the same information as) the _two_ Propositions (1) "_Some_ Members of the Subject are Members of the Predicate"; (2) "_No_ Members of the Subject are Members of the Class whose Differentia is _contradictory_ to that of the Predicate" </s>
<s> [Thus, the Proposition "_All_ bankers are rich men" is a _Double_ Proposition, and is equivalent to the _two_ Propositions (1) "_Some_ bankers are rich men"; (2) "_No_ bankers are _poor_ men".] pg019 Â§ 4 </s>
<s> _What is implied, in a Proposition of Relation, as to the Reality of its Terms?_ Note that the rules, here laid down, are _arbitrary_, and only apply to Part I of my "Symbolic Logic" </s>
<s> A Proposition of Relation, beginning with "Some", is henceforward to be understood as asserting that there are _some existing Things_, which, being Members of the Subject, are also Members of the Predicate; i.e </s>
<s> that _some existing Things_ are Members of _both_ Terms at once </s>
<s> Hence it is to be understood as implying that _each_ Term, taken by itself, is _Real_ </s>
<s> [Thus, the Proposition "Some rich men are invalids" is to be understood as asserting that _some existing Things_ are "rich invalids" </s>
<s> Hence it implies that _each_ of the two Classes, "rich men" and "invalids", taken by itself, is _Real_.] A Proposition of Relation, beginning with "No", is henceforward to be understood as asserting that there are _no existing Things_ which, being Members of the Subject, are also Members of the Predicate; i.e </s>
<s> that _no existing Things_ are Members of _both_ Terms at once </s>
<s> But this implies nothing as to the _Reality_ of either Term taken by itself </s>
<s> [Thus, the Proposition "No mermaids are milliners" is to be understood as asserting that _no existing Things_ are "mermaid-milliners" </s>
<s> But this implies nothing as to the _Reality_, or the _Unreality_, of either of the two Classes, "mermaids" and "milliners", taken by itself </s>
<s> In this case as it happens, the Subject is _Imaginary_, and the Predicate _Real_.] A Proposition of Relation, beginning with "All", contains (see Â§ 3) a similar Proposition beginning with "Some" </s>
<s> Hence it is to be understood as implying that _each_ Term, taken by itself, is _Real_ </s>
<s> [Thus, the Proposition "All hyÃ¦nas are savage animals" contains the Proposition "Some hyÃ¦nas are savage animals" </s>
<s> Hence it implies that _each_ of the two Classes, "hyÃ¦nas" and "savage animals", taken by itself, is _Real_.] pg020 Â§ 5 </s>
<s> _Translation of a Proposition of Relation into one or more Propositions of Existence._ We have seen that a Proposition of Relation, beginning with "Some," asserts that _some existing Things_, being Members of its Subject, are _also_ Members of its Predicate </s>
<s> Hence, it asserts that some existing Things are Members of _both_; i.e </s>
<s> it asserts that some existing Things are Members of the Class of Things which have _all_ the Attributes of the Subject and the Predicate </s>
<s> Hence, to translate it into a Proposition of Existence, we take "existing Things" as the new _Subject_, and Things, which have _all_ the Attributes of the Subject and the Predicate, as the new Predicate </s>
<s> Similarly for a Proposition of Relation beginning with "No" </s>
<s> A Proposition of Relation, beginning with "All", is (as shown in Â§ 3) equivalent to _two_ Propositions, one beginning with "Some" and the other with "No", each of which we now know how to translate </s>
<s> [Let us work a few Examples, to illustrate these Rules </s>
<s> (1) "Some apples are not ripe" </s>
<s> Here we arrange thus:-- "Some" _Sign of Quantity_ </s>
<s> "existing Things" _Subject_ </s>
<s> "are" _Copula_ </s>
<s> "not-ripe apples" _Predicate_ </s>
<s> or thus:-- "Some | existing Things | are | not-ripe apples" </s>
<s> pg021 (2) "Some farmers always grumble at the weather, whatever it may be" </s>
<s> Here we arrange thus:-- "Some | existing Things | are | farmers who always grumble at the weather, whatever it may be" </s>
<s> (3) "No lambs are accustomed to smoke cigars" </s>
<s> Here we arrange thus:-- "No | existing Things |are | lambs accustomed to smoke cigars" </s>
<s> (4) "None of my speculations have brought me as much as 5 per cent" </s>
<s> Here we arrange thus:-- "No | existing Things | are | speculations of mine, which have brought me as much as 5 per cent" </s>
<s> (5) "None but the brave deserve the fair" </s>
<s> Here we note, to begin with, that the phrase "none but the brave" is equivalent to "no not-brave men" </s>
<s> We then arrange thus:-- "No | existing Things | are | not-brave men deserving of the fair" </s>
<s> (6) "All bankers are rich men" </s>
<s> This is equivalent to the two Propositions "Some bankers are rich men" and "No bankers are poor men" </s>
<s> Here we arrange thus:-- "Some | existing Things | are | rich bankers"; and "No | existing Things | are | poor bankers".] [Work Examples Â§ =1=, 1-4 (p </s>
<s> 97).] pg022 BOOK III </s>

<s> _SYMBOLS AND CELLS._ First, let us suppose that the above Diagram is an enclosure assigned to a certain Class of Things, which we have selected as our 'Universe of Discourse' </s>
<s> or, more briefly, as our 'Univ' </s>
<s> [For example, we might say "Let Univ </s>
<s> be 'books'"; and we might imagine the Diagram to be a large table, assigned to all "books".] [The Reader is strongly advised, in reading this Chapter, _not_ to refer to the above Diagram, but to draw a large one for himself, _without any letters_, and to have it by him while he reads, and keep his finger on that particular _part_ of it, about which he is reading.] pg023 Secondly, let us suppose that we have selected a certain Adjunct, which we may call "x," and have divided the large Class, to which we have assigned the whole Diagram, into the two smaller Classes whose DifferentiÃ¦ are "x" and "not-x" (which we may call "x'"), and that we have assigned the _North_ Half of the Diagram to the one (which we may call "the Class of x-Things," or "the x-Class"), and the _South_ Half to the other (which we may call "the Class of x'-Things," or "the x'-Class") </s>
<s> [For example, we might say "Let x mean 'old,' so that x' will mean 'new'," and we might suppose that we had divided books into the two Classes whose DifferentiÃ¦ are "old" and "new," and had assigned the _North_ Half of the table to "_old_ books" and the _South_ Half to "_new_ books".] Thirdly, let us suppose that we have selected another Adjunct, which we may call "y", and have subdivided the x-Class into the two Classes whose DifferentiÃ¦ are "y" and "y'", and that we have assigned the North-_West_ Cell to the one (which we may call "the xy-Class"), and the North-_East_ Cell to the other (which we may call "the xy'-Class") </s>
<s> [For example, we might say "Let y mean 'English,' so that y' will mean 'foreign'", and we might suppose that we had subdivided "old books" into the two Classes whose DifferentiÃ¦ are "English" and "foreign", and had assigned the North-_West_ Cell to "old _English_ books", and the North-_East_ Cell to "old _foreign_ books".] Fourthly, let us suppose that we have subdivided the x'-Class in the same manner, and have assigned the South-_West_ Cell to the x'y-Class, and the South-_East_ Cell to the x'y'-Class </s>
<s> [For example, we might suppose that we had subdivided "new books" into the two Classes "new _English_ books" and "new _foreign_ books", and had assigned the South-_West_ Cell to the one, and the South-_East_ Cell to the other.] It is evident that, if we had begun by dividing for y and y', and had then subdivided for x and x', we should have got the _same_ four Classes </s>
<s> Hence we see that we have assigned the _West_ Half to the y-Class, and the _East_ Half to the y'-Class </s>
<s> pg024 [Thus, in the above Example, we should find that we had assigned the _West_ Half of the table to "_English_ books" and the _East_ Half to "_foreign_ books" </s>
<s> Â·-------------------Â· | old | old | | English | foreign | | books | books | |---------|---------| | new | new | | English | foreign | | books | books | Â·-------------------Â· We have, in fact, assigned the four Quarters of the table to four different Classes of books, as here shown.] The Reader should carefully remember that, in such a phrase as "the x-Things," the word "Things" means that particular _kind_ of Things, to which the whole Diagram has been assigned </s>
<s> [Thus, if we say "Let Univ </s>
<s> be 'books'," we mean that we have assigned the whole Diagram to "books" </s>
<s> In that case, if we took "x" to mean "old", the phrase "the x-Things" would mean "the old books".] The Reader should not go on to the next Chapter until he is _quite familiar_ with the _blank_ Diagram I have advised him to draw </s>
<s> He ought to be able to name, _instantly_, the _Adjunct_ assigned to any Compartment named in the right-hand column of the following Table </s>

<s> pg026 CHAPTER II </s>
<s> _COUNTERS._ Let us agree that a _Red_ Counter, placed within a Cell, shall mean "This Cell is _occupied_" (i.e </s>
<s> "There is at least _one_ Thing in it") </s>
<s> Let us also agree that a _Red_ Counter, placed on the partition between two Cells, shall mean "The Compartment, made up of these two Cells, is _occupied_; but it is not known _whereabouts_, in it, its occupants are" </s>
<s> Hence it may be understood to mean "At least _one_ of these two Cells is occupied: possibly _both_ are" </s>
<s> Our ingenious American cousins have invented a phrase to describe the condition of a man who has not yet made up his mind _which_ of two political parties he will join: such a man is said to be "=sitting on the fence=" </s>
<s> This phrase exactly describes the condition of the Red Counter </s>
<s> Let us also agree that a _Grey_ Counter, placed within a Cell, shall mean "This Cell is _empty_" (i.e </s>
<s> "There is _nothing_ in it") </s>
<s> [The Reader had better provide himself with 4 Red Counters and 5 Grey ones.] pg027 CHAPTER III </s>
<s> _REPRESENTATION OF PROPOSITIONS._ Â§ 1 </s>
<s> _Introductory._ Henceforwards, in stating such Propositions as "Some x-Things exist" or "No x-Things are y-Things", I shall omit the word "Things", which the Reader can supply for himself, and shall write them as "Some x exist" or "No x are y" </s>
<s> [Note that the word "Things" is here used with a special meaning, as explained at p </s>
<s> 23.] A Proposition, containing only _one_ of the Letters used as Symbols for Attributes, is said to be '=Uniliteral=' </s>
<s> [For example, "Some x exist", "No y' exist", &c.] A Proposition, containing _two_ Letters, is said to be ='Biliteral'= </s>
<s> [For example, "Some xy' exist", "No x' are y", &c.] A Proposition is said to be '=in terms of=' the Letters it contains, whether with or without accents </s>
<s> [Thus, "Some xy' exist", "No x' are y", &c., are said to be _in terms of_ x and y.] pg028 Â§ 2 </s>
<s> _Representation of Propositions of Existence._ Let us take, first, the Proposition "Some x exist" </s>
<s> [Note that this Proposition is (as explained at p </s>
<s> 12) equivalent to "Some existing Things are x-Things".] This tells us that there is at least _one_ Thing in the North Half; that is, that the North Half is _occupied_ </s>
<s> And this we can evidently represent by placing a _Red_ Counter (here represented by a _dotted_ circle) on the partition which divides the North Half </s>
<s> Â·-------Â· | (.) | |---|---| | | | Â·-------Â· [In the "books" example, this Proposition would be "Some old books exist".] Similarly we may represent the three similar Propositions "Some x' exist", "Some y exist", and "Some y' exist" </s>
<s> [The Reader should make out all these for himself </s>
<s> In the "books" example, these Propositions would be "Some new books exist", &c.] Let us take, next, the Proposition "No x exist" </s>
<s> This tells us that there is _nothing_ in the North Half; that is, that the North Half is _empty_; that is, that the North-West Cell and the North-East Cell are both of them _empty_ </s>
<s> And this we can represent by placing _two Grey_ Counters in the North Half, one in each Cell </s>
<s> Â·-------Â· |( )|( )| |---|---| | | | Â·-------Â· [The Reader may perhaps think that it would be enough to place a _Grey_ Counter on the partition in the North Half, and that, just as a _Red_ Counter, so placed, would mean "This Half is _occupied_", so a _Grey_ one would mean "This Half is _empty_" </s>
<s> This, however, would be a mistake </s>
<s> We have seen that a _Red_ Counter, so placed, would mean "At least _one_ of these two Cells is occupied: possibly _both_ are" </s>
<s> Hence a _Grey_ one would merely mean "At least _one_ of these two Cells is empty: possibly _both_ are" </s>
<s> But what we have to represent is, that both Cells are _certainly_ empty: and this can only be done by placing a _Grey_ Counter in _each_ of them </s>
<s> In the "books" example, this Proposition would be "No old books exist".] pg029 Similarly we may represent the three similar Propositions "No x' exist", "No y exist", and "No y' exist" </s>
<s> [The Reader should make out all these for himself </s>
<s> In the "books" example, these three Propositions would be "No new books exist", &c.] Let us take, next, the Proposition "Some xy exist" </s>
<s> This tells us that there is at least _one_ Thing in the North-West Cell; that is, that the North-West Cell is _occupied_ </s>
<s> And this we can represent by placing a _Red_ Counter in it </s>
<s> Â·-------Â· |(.)| | |---|---| | | | Â·-------Â· [In the "books" example, this Proposition would be "Some old English books exist".] Similarly we may represent the three similar Propositions "Some xy' exist", "Some x'y exist", and "Some x'y' exist" </s>
<s> [The Reader should make out all these for himself </s>
<s> In the "books" example, these three Propositions would be "Some old foreign books exist", &c.] Let us take, next, the Proposition "No xy exist" </s>
<s> This tells us that there is _nothing_ in the North-West Cell; that is, that the North-West Cell is _empty_ </s>
<s> And this we can represent by placing a _Grey_ Counter in it </s>
<s> Â·-------Â· |( )| | |---|---| | | | Â·-------Â· [In the "books" example, this Proposition would be "No old English books exist".] Similarly we may represent the three similar Propositions "No xy' exist", "No x'y exist", and "No x'y' exist" </s>
<s> [The Reader should make out all these for himself </s>
<s> In the "books" example, these three Propositions would be "No old foreign books exist", &c.] pg030 We have seen that the Proposition "No x exist" may be represented by placing _two Grey_ Counters in the North Half, one in each Cell </s>
<s> Â·-------Â· |( )|( )| |---|---| | | | Â·-------Â· We have also seen that these two _Grey_ Counters, taken _separately_, represent the two Propositions "No xy exist" and "No xy' exist" </s>
<s> Hence we see that the Proposition "No x exist" is a _Double_ Proposition, and is equivalent to the _two_ Propositions "No xy exist" and "No xy' exist" </s>
<s> [In the "books" example, this Proposition would be "No old books exist" </s>
<s> Hence this is a _Double_ Proposition, and is equivalent to the _two_ Propositions "No old _English_ books exist" and "No old _foreign_ books exist".] Â§ 3 </s>
<s> _Representation of Propositions of Relation._ Let us take, first, the Proposition "Some x are y" </s>
<s> This tells us that at least _one_ Thing, in the _North_ Half, is also in the _West_ Half </s>
<s> Hence it must be in the space _common_ to them, that is, in the _North-West Cell_ </s>
<s> Hence the North-West Cell is _occupied_ </s>
<s> And this we can represent by placing a _Red_ Counter in it </s>
<s> Â·-------Â· |(.)| | |---|---| | | | Â·-------Â· [Note that the _Subject_ of the Proposition settles which _Half_ we are to use; and that the _Predicate_ settles in which _portion_ of it we are to place the Red Counter </s>
<s> In the "books" example, this Proposition would be "Some old books are English".] Similarly we may represent the three similar Propositions "Some x are y'", "Some x' are y", and "Some x' are y'" </s>
<s> [The Reader should make out all these for himself </s>
<s> In the "books" example, these three Propositions would be "Some old books are foreign", &c.] pg031 Let us take, next, the Proposition "Some y are x" </s>
<s> This tells us that at least _one_ Thing, in the _West_ Half, is also in the _North_ Half </s>
<s> Hence it must be in the space _common_ to them, that is, in the _North-West Cell_ </s>
<s> Hence the North-West Cell is _occupied_ </s>
<s> And this we can represent by placing a _Red_ Counter in it </s>
<s> Â·-------Â· |(.)| | |---|---| | | | Â·-------Â· [In the "books" example, this Proposition would be "Some English books are old".] Similarly we may represent the three similar Propositions "Some y are x'", "Some y' are x", and "Some y' are x'" </s>
<s> [The Reader should make out all these for himself </s>
<s> In the "books" example, these three Propositions would be "Some English books are new", &c.] We see that this _one_ Diagram has now served to represent no less than _three_ Propositions, viz </s>
<s> (1) "Some xy exist; (2) Some x are y; (3) Some y are x" </s>
<s> Â·-------Â· |(.)| | |---|---| | | | Â·-------Â· Hence these three Propositions are equivalent </s>
<s> [In the "books" example, these Propositions would be (1) "Some old English books exist; (2) Some old books are English; (3) Some English books are old".] The two equivalent Propositions, "Some x are y" and "Some y are x", are said to be '=Converse=' to each other; and the Process, of changing one into the other, is called '=Converting=', or '=Conversion=' </s>
<s> [For example, if we were told to convert the Proposition "Some apples are not ripe," we should first choose our Univ </s>
<s> (say "fruit"), and then complete the Proposition, by supplying the Substantive "fruit" in the Predicate, so that it would be "Some apples are not-ripe fruit"; and we should then convert it by interchanging its Terms, so that it would be "Some not-ripe fruit are apples".] pg032 Similarly we may represent the three similar Trios of equivalent Propositions; the whole Set of _four_ Trios being as follows:-- (1) "Some xy exist"Â =Â "Some x are y"Â =Â "Some y are x" </s>
<s> (2) "Some xy' exist"Â =Â "Some x are y'"Â =Â "Some y' are x" </s>
<s> (3) "Some x'y exist"Â =Â "Some x' are y"Â =Â "Some y are x'" </s>
<s> (4) "Some x'y' exist"Â =Â "Some x' are y'"Â =Â "Some y' are x'" </s>
<s> Let us take, next, the Proposition "No x are y" </s>
<s> This tell us that no Thing, in the _North_ Half, is also in the _West_ Half </s>
<s> Hence there is _nothing_ in the space _common_ to them, that is, in the _North-West Cell_ </s>
<s> Hence the North-West Cell is _empty_ </s>
<s> And this we can represent by placing a _Grey_ Counter in it </s>
<s> Â·-------Â· |( )| | |---|---| | | | Â·-------Â· [In the "books" example, this Proposition would be "No old books are English".] Similarly we may represent the three similar Propositions "No x are y'", and "No x' are y", and "No x' are y'" </s>
<s> [The Reader should make out all these for himself </s>
<s> In the "books" example, these three Propositions would be "No old books are foreign", &c.] Let us take, next, the Proposition "No y are x" </s>
<s> This tells us that no Thing, in the _West_ Half, is also in the _North_ Half </s>
<s> Hence there is _nothing_ in the space _common_ to them, that is, in the _North-West Cell_ </s>
<s> That is, the North-West Cell is _empty_ </s>
<s> And this we can represent by placing a _Grey_ Counter in it </s>
<s> Â·-------Â· |( )| | |---|---| | | | Â·-------Â· [In the "books" example, this Proposition would be "No English books are old".] Similarly we may represent the three similar Propositions "No y are x'", "No y' are x", and "No y' are x'" </s>
<s> [The Reader should make out all these for himself </s>
<s> In the "books" example, these three Propositions would be "No English books are new", &c.] pg033 Â·-------Â· |( )| | |---|---| | | | Â·-------Â· We see that this _one_ Diagram has now served to present no less than _three_ Propositions, viz </s>
<s> (1) "No xy exist; (2) No x are y; (3) No y are x" </s>
<s> Hence these three Propositions are equivalent </s>
<s> [In the "books" example, these Propositions would be (1) "No old English books exist; (2) No old books are English; (3) No English books are old".] The two equivalent Propositions, "No x are y" and "No y are x", are said to be 'Converse' to each other </s>
<s> [For example, if we were told to convert the Proposition "No porcupines are talkative", we should first choose our Univ </s>
<s> (say "animals"), and then complete the Proposition, by supplying the Substantive "animals" in the Predicate, so that it would be "No porcupines are talkative animals", and we should then convert it, by interchanging its Terms, so that it would be "No talkative animals are porcupines".] Similarly we may represent the three similar Trios of equivalent Propositions; the whole Set of _four_ Trios being as follows:-- (1) "No xy exist"Â =Â "No x are y"Â =Â "No y are x" </s>
<s> (2) "No xy' exist"Â =Â "No x are y'"Â =Â "No y' are x" </s>
<s> (3) "No x'y exist"Â =Â "No x' are y"Â =Â "No y are x'" </s>
<s> (4) "No x'y' exist"Â =Â "No x' are y'"Â =Â "No y' are x'" </s>
<s> Let us take, next, the Proposition "All x are y" </s>
<s> We know (see p </s>
<s> 17) that this is a _Double_ Proposition, and equivalent to the _two_ Propositions "Some x are y" and "No x are y'", each of which we already know how to represent </s>
<s> Â·-------Â· |(.)|( )| |---|---| | | | Â·-------Â· [Note that the _Subject_ of the given Proposition settles which _Half_ we are to use; and that its _Predicate_ settles in which _portion_ of that Half we are to place the Red Counter.] pg034 TABLE II </s>

<s> _INTERPRETATION OF BILITERAL DIAGRAM WHEN MARKED WITH COUNTERS._ The Diagram is supposed to be set before us, with certain Counters placed upon it; and the problem is to find out what Proposition, or Propositions, the Counters represent </s>
<s> As the process is simply the reverse of that discussed in the previous Chapter, we can avail ourselves of the results there obtained, as far as they go </s>
<s> First, let us suppose that we find a _Red_ Counter placed in the North-West Cell </s>
<s> Â·-------Â· |(.)| | |---|---| | | | Â·-------Â· We know that this represents each of the Trio of equivalent Propositions "Some xy exist"Â =Â "Some x are y"Â =Â "Some y are x" </s>
<s> Similarly we may interpret a _Red_ Counter, when placed in the North-East, or South-West, or South-East Cell </s>
<s> Next, let us suppose that we find a _Grey_ Counter placed in the North-West Cell </s>
<s> Â·-------Â· |( )| | |---|---| | | | Â·-------Â· We know that this represents each of the Trio of equivalent Propositions "No xy exist"Â =Â "No x are y"Â =Â "No y are x" </s>
<s> Similarly we may interpret a _Grey_ Counter, when placed in the North-East, or South-West, or South-East Cell </s>
<s> pg037 Next, let us suppose that we find a _Red_ Counter placed on the partition which divides the North Half </s>
<s> Â·-------Â· | (.) | |---|---| | | | Â·-------Â· We know that this represents the Proposition "Some x exist" </s>
<s> Similarly we may interpret a _Red_ Counter, when placed on the partition which divides the South, or West, or East Half </s>
<s> * * * * * Next, let us suppose that we find _two Red_ Counters placed in the North Half, one in each Cell </s>
<s> Â·-------Â· |(.)|(.)| |---|---| | | | Â·-------Â· We know that this represents the _Double_ Proposition "Some x are y and some are y'" </s>
<s> Similarly we may interpret _two Red_ Counters, when placed in the South, or West, or East Half </s>
<s> * * * * * Next, let us suppose that we find _two Grey_ Counters placed in the North Half, one in each Cell </s>
<s> Â·-------Â· |( )|( )| |---|---| | | | Â·-------Â· We know that this represents the Proposition "No x exist" </s>
<s> Similarly we may interpret _two Grey_ Counters, when placed in the South, or West, or East Half </s>
<s> * * * * * Lastly, let us suppose that we find a _Red_ and a _Grey_ Counter placed in the North Half, the _Red_ in the North-_West_ Cell, and the _Grey_ in the North-_East_ Cell </s>
<s> Â·-------Â· |(.)|( )| |---|---| | | | Â·-------Â· We know that this represents the Proposition, "All x are y" </s>
<s> [Note that the _Half_, occupied by the two Counters, settles what is to be the _Subject_ of the Proposition, and that the _Cell_, occupied by the _Red_ Counter, settles what is to be its _Predicate_.] pg038 Similarly we may interpret a _Red_ and a _Grey_ counter, when placed in any one of the seven similar positions Red in North-East, Grey in North-West; Red in South-West, Grey in South-East; Red in South-East, Grey in South-West; Red in North-West, Grey in South-West; Red in South-West, Grey in North-West; Red in North-East, Grey in South-East; Red in South-East, Grey in North-East </s>
<s> Once more the genial friend must be appealed to, and requested to examine the Reader on Tables II and III, and to make him not only _represent_ Propositions, but also _interpret_ Diagrams when marked with Counters </s>

<s> _SYMBOLS AND CELLS._ First, let us suppose that the above _left_-hand Diagram is the Biliteral Diagram that we have been using in Book III., and that we change it into a _Triliteral_ Diagram by drawing an _Inner Square_, so as to divide each of its 4 Cells into 2 portions, thus making 8 Cells altogether </s>
<s> The _right_-hand Diagram shows the result </s>
<s> [The Reader is strongly advised, in reading this Chapter, _not_ to refer to the above Diagrams, but to make a large copy of the right-hand one for himself, _without any letters_, and to have it by him while he reads, and keep his finger on that particular _part_ of it, about which he is reading.] pg040 Secondly, let us suppose that we have selected a certain Adjunct, which we may call "m", and have subdivided the xy-Class into the two Classes whose DifferentiÃ¦ are m and m', and that we have assigned the N.W </s>
<s> _Inner_ Cell to the one (which we may call "the Class of xym-Things", or "the xym-Class"), and the N.W </s>
<s> _Outer_ Cell to the other (which we may call "the Class of xym'-Things", or "the xym'-Class") </s>
<s> [Thus, in the "books" example, we might say "Let m mean 'bound', so that m' will mean 'unbound'", and we might suppose that we had subdivided the Class "old English books" into the two Classes, "old English bound books" and "old English unbound books", and had assigned the N.W </s>
<s> _Inner_ Cell to the one, and the N.W </s>
<s> _Outer_ Cell to the other.] Thirdly, let us suppose that we have subdivided the xy'-Class, the x'y-Class, and the x'y'-Class in the same manner, and have, in each case, assigned the _Inner_ Cell to the Class possessing the Attribute m, and the _Outer_ Cell to the Class possessing the Attribute m' </s>
<s> [Thus, in the "books" example, we might suppose that we had subdivided the "new English books" into the two Classes, "new English bound books" and "new English unbound books", and had assigned the S.W </s>
<s> _Inner_ Cell to the one, and the S.W </s>
<s> _Outer_ Cell to the other.] It is evident that we have now assigned the _Inner Square_ to the m-Class, and the _Outer Border_ to the m'-Class </s>
<s> [Thus, in the "books" example, we have assigned the _Inner Square_ to "bound books" and the _Outer Border_ to "unbound books".] When the Reader has made himself familiar with this Diagram, he ought to be able to find, in a moment, the Compartment assigned to a particular _pair_ of Attributes, or the Cell assigned to a particular _trio_ of Attributes </s>
<s> The following Rules will help him in doing this:-- (1) Arrange the Attributes in the order x, y, m </s>
<s> pg041 (2) Take the _first_ of them and find the Compartment assigned to it </s>
<s> (3) Then take the _second_, and find what _portion_ of that compartment is assigned to it </s>
<s> (4) Treat the _third_, if there is one, in the same way </s>
<s> [For example, suppose we have to find the Compartment assigned to ym </s>
<s> We say to ourselves "y has the _West_ Half; and m has the _Inner_ portion of that West Half" </s>
<s> Again, suppose we have to find the Cell assigned to x'ym' </s>
<s> We say to ourselves "x' has the _South_ Half; y has the _West_ portion of that South Half, i.e </s>
<s> has the _South-West Quarter_; and m' has the _Outer_ portion of that South-West Quarter".] The Reader should now get his genial friend to question him on the Table given on the next page, in the style of the following specimen-Dialogue </s>

<s> _REPRESENTATION OF PROPOSITIONS IN TERMS OF x AND m, OR OF y AND m._ Â§ 1 </s>
<s> _Representation of Propositions of Existence in terms of x and m, or of y and m._ Let us take, first, the Proposition "Some xm exist" </s>
<s> [Note that the _full_ meaning of this Proposition is (as explained at p </s>
<s> 12) "Some existing Things are xm-Things".] This tells us that there is at least _one_ Thing in the Inner portion of the North Half; that is, that this Compartment is _occupied_ </s>
<s> And this we can evidently represent by placing a _Red_ Counter on the partition which divides it </s>
<s> Â·---------------Â· | | | | Â·---|---Â· | | | (.) | | |---|---|---|---| | | | | | | Â·---|---Â· | | | | Â·---------------Â· [In the "books" example, this Proposition would mean "Some old bound books exist" (or "There are some old bound books").] Similarly we may represent the seven similar Propositions, "Some xm' exist", "Some x'm exist", "Some x'm' exist", "Some ym exist", "Some ym' exist", "Some y'm exist", and "Some y'm' exist" </s>
<s> pg044 Let us take, next, the Proposition "No xm exist" </s>
<s> This tells us that there is _nothing_ in the Inner portion of the North Half; that is, that this Compartment is _empty_ </s>
<s> And this we can represent by placing _two Grey_ Counters in it, one in each Cell </s>
<s> Â·---------------Â· | | | | Â·---|---Â· | | |( )|( )| | |---|---|---|---| | | | | | | Â·---|---Â· | | | | Â·---------------Â· Similarly we may represent the seven similar Propositions, in terms of x and m, or of y and m, viz </s>
<s> "No xm' exist", "No x'm exist", &c </s>
<s> * * * * * These sixteen Propositions of Existence are the only ones that we shall have to represent on this Diagram </s>

<s> _REPRESENTATION OF TWO PROPOSITIONS OF RELATION, ONE IN TERMS OF x AND m, AND THE OTHER IN TERMS OF y AND m, ON THE SAME DIAGRAM._ The Reader had better now begin to draw little Diagrams for himself, and to mark them with the Digits "I" and "O", instead of using the Board and Counters: he may put a "I" to represent a _Red_ Counter (this may be interpreted to mean "There is at least _one_ Thing here"), and a "O" to represent a _Grey_ Counter (this may be interpreted to mean "There is _nothing_ here") </s>
<s> The Pair of Propositions, that we shall have to represent, will always be, one in terms of x and m, and the other in terms of y and m </s>
<s> When we have to represent a Proposition beginning with "All", we break it up into the _two_ Propositions to which it is equivalent </s>
<s> When we have to represent, on the same Diagram, Propositions, of which some begin with "Some" and others with "No", we represent the _negative_ ones _first_ </s>
<s> This will sometimes save us from having to put a "I" "on a fence" and afterwards having to shift it into a Cell </s>
<s> [Let us work a few examples </s>
<s> (1) "No x are m'; No y' are m" </s>
<s> Let us first represent "No x are m'" </s>
<s> This gives us Diagram a </s>
<s> Then, representing "No y' are m" on the same Diagram, we get Diagram b </s>
<s> pg051 a b Â·---------------Â· Â·---------------Â· |(O) | (O)| |(O) | (O)| | Â·---|---Â· | | Â·---|---Â· | | | | | | | | |(O)| | |---|---|---|---| |---|---|---|---| | | | | | | | |(O)| | | Â·---|---Â· | | Â·---|---Â· | | | | | | | Â·---------------Â· Â·---------------Â· (2) "Some m are x; No m are y" </s>
<s> If, neglecting the Rule, we were begin with "Some m are x", we should get Diagram a </s>
<s> And if we were then to take "No m are y", which tells us that the Inner N.W </s>
<s> Cell is _empty_, we should be obliged to take the "I" off the fence (as it no longer has the choice of _two_ Cells), and to put it into the Inner N.E </s>
<s> Cell, as in Diagram c </s>
<s> This trouble may be saved by beginning with "No m are y", as in Diagram b </s>
<s> And _now_, when we take "Some m are x", there is no fence to sit on </s>
<s> The "I" has to go, at once, into the N.E </s>
<s> Cell, as in Diagram c </s>
<s> a b c Â·---------------Â· Â·---------------Â· Â·---------------Â· | | | | | | | | | | Â·---|---Â· | | Â·---|---Â· | | Â·---|---Â· | | | (I) | | | |(O)| | | | |(O)|(I)| | |---|---|---|---| |---|---|---|---| |---|---|---|---| | | | | | | |(O)| | | | |(O)| | | | Â·---|---Â· | | Â·---|---Â· | | Â·---|---Â· | | | | | | | | | | Â·---------------Â· Â·---------------Â· Â·---------------Â· (3) "No x' are m'; All m are y" </s>

<s> _INTERPRETATION, IN TERMS OF x AND y, OF TRILITERAL DIAGRAM, WHEN MARKED WITH COUNTERS OR DIGITS._ The problem before us is, given a marked Triliteral Diagram, to ascertain _what_ Propositions of Relation, in terms of x and y, are represented on it </s>
<s> The best plan, for a _beginner_, is to draw a _Biliteral_ Diagram alongside of it, and to transfer, from the one to the other, all the information he can </s>
<s> He can then read off, from the Biliteral Diagram, the required Propositions </s>
<s> After a little practice, he will be able to dispense with the Biliteral Diagram, and to read off the result from the Triliteral Diagram itself </s>
<s> To _transfer_ the information, observe the following Rules:-- (1) Examine the N.W </s>
<s> Quarter of the Triliteral Diagram </s>
<s> (2) If it contains a "I", in _either_ Cell, it is certainly _occupied_, and you may mark the N.W </s>
<s> Quarter of the Biliteral Diagram with a "I" </s>
<s> (3) If it contains _two_ "O"s, one in _each_ Cell, it is certainly _empty_, and you may mark the N.W </s>
<s> Quarter of the Biliteral Diagram with a "O" </s>
<s> pg054 (4) Deal in the same way with the N.E., the S.W., and the S.E </s>
<s> Quarter </s>
<s> [Let us take, as examples, the results of the four Examples worked in the previous Chapters </s>
