<s> SYLLOGISMS </s>
<s> CHAPTER I </s>
<s> _INTRODUCTORY_ When a Trio of Biliteral Propositions of Relation is such that (1) all their six Terms are Species of the same Genus, (2) every two of them contain between them a Pair of codivisional Classes, (3) the three Propositions are so related that, if the first two were true, the third would be true, the Trio is called a '=Syllogism='; the Genus, of which each of the six Terms is a Species, is called its ='Universe of Discourse=', or, more briefly, its '=Univ.='; the first two Propositions are called its '=Premisses=', and the third its '=Conclusion='; also the Pair of codivisional Terms in the Premisses are called its '=Eliminands=', and the other two its '=Retinends=' </s>
<s> The Conclusion of a Syllogism is said to be '=consequent=' from its Premisses: hence it is usual to prefix to it the word "Therefore" (or the Symbol "'.".) </s>
<s> pg057 [Note that the 'Eliminands' are so called because they are _eliminated_, and do not appear in the Conclusion; and that the 'Retinends' are so called because they are _retained_, and _do_ appear in the Conclusion </s>
<s> Note also that the question, whether the Conclusion is or is not _consequent_ from the Premisses, is not affected by the _actual_ truth or falsity of any of the Trio, but depends entirely on their _relationship to each other_ </s>
<s> As a specimen-Syllogism, let us take the Trio "No x-Things are m-Things; No y-Things are m'-Things </s>
<s> No x-Things are y-Things" </s>
<s> which we may write, as explained at p </s>
<s> 26, thus:-- "No x are m; No y are m' </s>
<s> No x are y" </s>
<s> Here the first and second contain the Pair of codivisional Classes m and m'; the first and third contain the Pair x and x; and the second and third contain the Pair y and y </s>
<s> Also the three Propositions are (as we shall see hereafter) so related that, if the first two were true, the third would also be true </s>
<s> Hence the Trio is a _Syllogism_; the two Propositions, "No x are m" and "No y are m'", are its _Premisses_; the Proposition "No x are y" is its _Conclusion_; the Terms m and m' are its _Eliminands_; and the Terms x and y are its _Retinends_ </s>
<s> Hence we may write it thus:-- "No x are m; No y are m' </s>
<s> '. </s>
<s> No x are y" </s>
<s> As a second specimen, let us take the Trio "All cats understand French; Some chickens are cats </s>
<s> Some chickens understand French" </s>
<s> These, put into normal form, are "All cats are creatures understanding French; Some chickens are cats </s>
<s> Some chickens are creatures understanding French" </s>
<s> Here all the six Terms are Species of the Genus "creatures" </s>
<s> Also the first and second Propositions contain the Pair of codivisional Classes "cats" and "cats"; the first and third contain the Pair "creatures understanding French" and "creatures understanding French"; and the second and third contain the Pair "chickens" and "chickens" </s>
<s> pg058 Also the three Propositions are (as we shall see at p </s>
<s> 64) so related that, if the first two were true, the third would be true </s>
<s> (The first two are, as it happens, _not_ strictly true in _our_ planet </s>
<s> But there is nothing to hinder them from being true in some _other_ planet, say _Mars_ or _Jupiter_--in which case the third would _also_ be true in that planet, and its inhabitants would probably engage chickens as nursery-governesses </s>
<s> They would thus secure a singular _contingent_ privilege, unknown in England, namely, that they would be able, at any time when provisions ran short, to utilise the nursery-governess for the nursery-dinner!) Hence the Trio is a _Syllogism_; the Genus "creatures" is its 'Univ'.; the two Propositions, "All cats understand French" and "Some chickens are cats", are its _Premisses_, the Proposition "Some chickens understand French" is its _Conclusion_; the Terms "cats" and "cats" are its _Eliminands_; and the Terms, "creatures understanding French" and "chickens", are its _Retinends_ </s>
<s> Hence we may write it thus:-- "All cats understand French; Some chickens are cats; '. </s>
<s> Some chickens understand French".] pg059 CHAPTER II </s>
<s> _PROBLEMS IN SYLLOGISMS._ Â§ 1 </s>
<s> _Introductory._ When the Terms of a Proposition are represented by _words_, it is said to be '=concrete='; when by _letters_, '=abstract=' </s>
<s> To translate a Proposition from concrete into abstract form, we fix on a Univ., and regard each Term as a _Species_ of it, and we choose a letter to represent its _Differentia_ </s>
<s> [For example, suppose we wish to translate "Some soldiers are brave" into abstract form </s>
<s> We may take "men" as Univ., and regard "soldiers" and "brave men" as _Species_ of the _Genus_ "men"; and we may choose x to represent the peculiar Attribute (say "military") of "soldiers," and y to represent "brave" </s>
<s> Then the Proposition may be written "Some military men are brave men"; _i.e._ "Some x-men are y-men"; _i.e._ (omitting "men," as explained at p </s>
<s> 26) "Some x are y" </s>
<s> In practice, we should merely say "Let Univ </s>
<s> be "men", xÂ =Â soldiers, yÂ =Â brave", and at once translate "Some soldiers are brave" into "Some x are y".] The Problems we shall have to solve are of two kinds, viz </s>
<s> (1) "Given a Pair of Propositions of Relation, which contain between them a pair of codivisional Classes, and which are proposed as Premisses: to ascertain what Conclusion, if any, is consequent from them" </s>
<s> (2) "Given a Trio of Propositions of Relation, of which every two contain a pair of codivisional Classes, and which are proposed as a Syllogism: to ascertain whether the proposed Conclusion is consequent from the proposed Premisses, and, if so, whether it is _complete_" </s>
<s> These Problems we will discuss separately </s>
<s> pg060 Â§ 2 </s>
<s> _Given a Pair of Propositions of Relation, which contain between them a pair of codivisional Classes, and which are proposed as Premisses: to ascertain what Conclusion, if any, is consequent from them._ The Rules, for doing this, are as follows:-- (1) Determine the 'Universe of Discourse' </s>
<s> (2) Construct a Dictionary, making m and m (or m and m') represent the pair of codivisional Classes, and x (or x') and y (or y') the other two </s>
<s> (3) Translate the proposed Premisses into abstract form </s>
<s> (4) Represent them, together, on a Triliteral Diagram </s>
<s> (5) Ascertain what Proposition, if any, in terms of x and y, is _also_ represented on it </s>
<s> (6) Translate this into concrete form </s>
<s> It is evident that, if the proposed Premisses were true, this other Proposition would _also_ be true </s>
<s> Hence it is a _Conclusion_ consequent from the proposed Premisses </s>
<s> [Let us work some examples </s>
<s> (1) "No son of mine is dishonest; People always treat an honest man with respect" </s>
<s> Taking "men" as Univ., we may write these as follows:-- "No sons of mine are dishonest men; All honest men are men treated with respect" </s>
<s> We can now construct our Dictionary, viz </s>
<s> mÂ =Â honest; xÂ =Â sons of mine; yÂ =Â treated with respect </s>
<s> (Note that the expression "xÂ =Â sons of mine" is an abbreviated form of "xÂ =Â the Differentia of 'sons of mine', when regarded as a Species of 'men'".) The next thing is to translate the proposed Premisses into abstract form, as follows:-- "No x are m'; All m are y" </s>
<s> pg061 Next, by the process described at p </s>
<s> 50, we represent these on a Triliteral Diagram, thus:-- Â·---------------Â· |(O) | (O)| | Â·---|---Â· | | | |(O)| | |---|(I)|---|---| | | |(O)| | | Â·---|---Â· | | | | Â·---------------Â· Next, by the process described at p </s>
<s> 53, we transfer to a Biliteral Diagram all the information we can </s>
<s> Â·-------Â· | |(O)| |---|---| | | | Â·-------Â· The result we read as "No x are y'" or as "No y' are x," whichever we prefer </s>
<s> So we refer to our Dictionary, to see which will look best; and we choose "No x are y'", which, translated into concrete form, is "No son of mine fails to be treated with respect" </s>
<s> (2) "All cats understand French; Some chickens are cats" </s>
<s> Taking "creatures" as Univ., we write these as follows:-- "All cats are creatures understanding French; Some chickens are cats" </s>
<s> We can now construct our Dictionary, viz </s>
<s> mÂ =Â cats; xÂ =Â understanding French; yÂ =Â chickens </s>
<s> The proposed Premisses, translated into abstract form, are "All m are x; Some y are m" </s>
<s> In order to represent these on a Triliteral Diagram, we break up the first into the two Propositions to which it is equivalent, and thus get the _three_ Propositions (1) "Some m are x; (2) No m are x'; (3) Some y are m" </s>
<s> The Rule, given at p </s>
<s> 50, would make us take these in the order 2, 1, 3 </s>
<s> This, however, would produce the result Â·-----------------Â· | | | | Â·----|----Â· | | |(I)(I) | | | |----|----| | | |(O) | (O)| | | Â·----|----Â· | | | | Â·-----------------Â· pg062 So it would be better to take them in the order 2, 3, 1 </s>
<s> Nos </s>
<s> (2) and (3) give us the result here shown; and now we need not trouble about No </s>
<s> (1), as the Proposition "Some m are x" is _already_ represented on the Diagram </s>

<s> _Given a Trio of Propositions of Relation, of which every two contain a Pair of codivisional Classes, and which are proposed as a Syllogism; to ascertain whether the proposed Conclusion is consequent from the proposed Premisses, and, if so, whether it is complete._ The Rules, for doing this, are as follows:-- (1) Take the proposed Premisses, and ascertain, by the process described at p </s>
<s> 60, what Conclusion, if any, is consequent from them </s>
<s> (2) If there be _no_ Conclusion, say so </s>
<s> (3) If there _be_ a Conclusion, compare it with the proposed Conclusion, and pronounce accordingly </s>
<s> I will now work out, in their briefest form, as models for the Reader to imitate in working examples, six Problems </s>

<s> THE METHOD OF SUBSCRIPTS </s>
<s> CHAPTER I </s>
<s> _INTRODUCTORY._ Let us agree that "x_{1}" shall mean "Some existing Things have the Attribute x", i.e </s>
<s> (more briefly) "Some x exist"; also that "xy_{1}" shall mean "Some xy exist", and so on </s>
<s> Such a Proposition may be called an '=Entity=' </s>
<s> [Note that, when there are _two_ letters in the expression, it does not in the least matter which stands _first_: "xy_{1}" and "yx_{1}" mean exactly the same.] Also that "x_{0}" shall mean "No existing Things have the Attribute x", i.e </s>
<s> (more briefly) "No x exist"; also that "xy_{0}" shall mean "No xy exist", and so on </s>
<s> Such a Proposition may be called a '=Nullity=' </s>
<s> Also that "+" shall mean "and" </s>
<s> [Thus "ab_{1} + cd_{0}" means "Some ab exist and no cd exist".] Also that "Â¶" shall mean "would, if true, prove" </s>
<s> [Thus, "x_{0} Â¶ xy_{0}" means "The Proposition 'No x exist' would, if true, prove the Proposition 'No xy exist'".] When two Letters are both of them accented, or both _not_ accented, they are said to have '=Like Signs=', or to be '=Like=': when one is accented, and the other not, they are said to have '=Unlike Signs=', or to be '=Unlike=' </s>
<s> pg071 CHAPTER II </s>
<s> _REPRESENTATION OF PROPOSITIONS OF RELATION._ Let us take, first, the Proposition "Some x are y" </s>
<s> This, we know, is equivalent to the Proposition of Existence "Some xy exist" </s>
<s> (See p </s>
<s> 31.) Hence it may be represented by the expression "xy_{1}" </s>
<s> The Converse Proposition "Some y are x" may of course be represented by the _same_ expression, viz </s>
<s> "xy_{1}" </s>
<s> Similarly we may represent the three similar Pairs of Converse Propositions, viz.-- "Some x are y'" Â =Â "Some y' are x", "Some x' are y" Â =Â "Some y are x'", "Some x' are y'"Â =Â "Some y' are x'" </s>
<s> Let us take, next, the Proposition "No x are y" </s>
<s> This, we know, is equivalent to the Proposition of Existence "No xy exist" </s>
<s> (See p </s>
<s> 33.) Hence it may be represented by the expression "xy_{0}" </s>
<s> The Converse Proposition "No y are x" may of course be represented by the _same_ expression, viz </s>
<s> "xy_{0}" </s>
<s> Similarly we may represent the three similar Pairs of Converse Propositions, viz.-- "No x are y'" Â =Â "No y' are x", "No x' are y" Â =Â "No y are x'", "No x' are y'"Â =Â "No y' are x'" </s>
<s> pg072 Let us take, next, the Proposition "All x are y" </s>
<s> Now it is evident that the Double Proposition of Existence "Some x exist and no xy' exist" tells us that _some_ x-Things exist, but that _none_ of them have the Attribute y': that is, it tells us that _all_ of them have the Attribute y: that is, it tells us that "All x are y" </s>
<s> Also it is evident that the expression "x_{1} + xy'_{0}" represents this Double Proposition </s>
<s> Hence it also represents the Proposition "All x are y" </s>
<s> [The Reader will perhaps be puzzled by the statement that the Proposition "All x are y" is equivalent to the Double Proposition "Some x exist and no xy' exist," remembering that it was stated, at p </s>
<s> 33, to be equivalent to the Double Proposition "Some x are y and no x are y'" (i.e </s>
<s> "Some xy exist and no xy' exist") </s>
<s> The explanation is that the Proposition "Some xy exist" contains _superfluous information_ </s>
<s> "Some x exist" is enough for our purpose.] This expression may be written in a shorter form, viz </s>
<s> "x_{1}y'_{0}", since _each_ Subscript takes effect back to the _beginning_ of the expression </s>
<s> Similarly we may represent the seven similar Propositions "All x are y'", "All x' are y", "All x' are y'", "All y are x", "All y are x'", "All y' are x", and "All y' are x'" </s>
<s> [The Reader should make out all these for himself.] It will be convenient to remember that, in translating a Proposition, beginning with "All", from abstract form into subscript form, or _vice versÃ¢_, the Predicate _changes sign_ (that is, changes from positive to negative, or else from negative to positive) </s>
<s> [Thus, the Proposition "All y are x'" becomes "y_{1}x_{0}", where the Predicate changes from x' to x </s>
<s> Again, the expression "x'_{1}y'_{0}" becomes "All x' are y", where the Predicate changes for y' to y.] pg073 CHAPTER III </s>
<s> _SYLLOGISMS._ Â§ 1 </s>
<s> _Representation of Syllogisms._ We already know how to represent each of the three Propositions of a Syllogism in subscript form </s>
<s> When that is done, all we need, besides, is to write the three expressions in a row, with "+" between the Premisses, and "Â¶" before the Conclusion </s>
<s> [Thus the Syllogism "No x are m'; All m are y </s>
<s> '. </s>
<s> No x are y'" </s>
<s> may be represented thus:-- xm'_{0} + m_{1}y'_{0} Â¶ xy'_{0} When a Proposition has to be translated from concrete form into subscript form, the Reader will find it convenient, just at first, to translate it into _abstract_ form, and _thence_ into subscript form </s>
<s> But, after a little practice, he will find it quite easy to go straight from concrete form to subscript form.] pg074 Â§ 2 </s>
<s> _FormulÃ¦ for solving Problems in Syllogisms._ When once we have found, by Diagrams, the Conclusion to a given Pair of Premisses, and have represented the Syllogism in subscript form, we have a _Formula_, by which we can at once find, without having to use Diagrams again, the Conclusion to any _other_ Pair of Premisses having the _same_ subscript forms </s>
<s> [Thus, the expression xm_{0} + ym'_{0} Â¶ xy_{0} is a Formula, by which we can find the Conclusion to any Pair of Premisses whose subscript forms are xm_{0} + ym'_{0} For example, suppose we had the Pair of Propositions "No gluttons are healthy; No unhealthy men are strong" </s>
<s> proposed as Premisses </s>
<s> Taking "men" as our 'Universe', and making mÂ =Â healthy; xÂ =Â gluttons; yÂ =Â strong; we might translate the Pair into abstract form, thus:-- "No x are m; No m' are y" </s>
<s> These, in subscript form, would be xm_{0} + m'y_{0} which are identical with those in our _Formula_ </s>
<s> Hence we at once know the Conclusion to be xy_{0} that is, in abstract form, "No x are y"; that is, in concrete form, "No gluttons are strong".] I shall now take three different forms of Pairs of Premisses, and work out their Conclusions, once for all, by Diagrams; and thus obtain some useful FormulÃ¦ </s>
<s> I shall call them "Fig </s>
<s> I", "Fig </s>
<s> II", and "Fig </s>
<s> III" </s>
<s> pg075 Fig </s>
<s> I </s>
<s> This includes any Pair of Premisses which are both of them Nullities, and which contain Unlike Eliminands </s>
<s> The simplest case is Â·---------------Â· Â·-------Â· xm_{0} + ym'_{0} |(O) | | |(O)| | | Â·---|---Â· | |---|---| | |(O)|(O)| | | | | |---|---|---|---| Â·-------Â· | | | | | | Â·---|---Â· | '. </s>
<s> xy_{0} |(O) | | Â·---------------Â· In this case we see that the Conclusion is a Nullity, and that the Retinends have kept their Signs </s>
<s> And we should find this Rule to hold good with _any_ Pair of Premisses which fulfil the given conditions </s>
<s> [The Reader had better satisfy himself of this, by working out, on Diagrams, several varieties, such as m_{1}x_{0} + ym'_{0} (which Â¶ xy_{0}) xm'_{0} + m_{1}y_{0} (which Â¶ xy_{0}) x'm_{0} + ym'_{0} (which Â¶ x'y_{0}) m'_{1}x'_{0} + m_{1}y'_{0} (which Â¶ x'y'_{0}).] If either Retinend is asserted in the _Premisses_ to exist, of course it may be so asserted in the _Conclusion_ </s>
<s> Hence we get two _Variants_ of Fig </s>
<s> I, viz </s>
<s> (a) where _one_ Retinend is so asserted; (b) where _both_ are so asserted </s>
<s> [The Reader had better work out, on Diagrams, examples of these two Variants, such as m_{1}x_{0} + y_{1}m'_{0} (which proves y_{1}x_{0}) x_{1}m'_{0} + m_{1}y_{0} (which proves x_{1}y_{0}) x'_{1}m_{0} + y_{1}m'_{0} (which proves x'_{1}y_{0} + y_{1}x'_{0}).] The Formula, to be remembered, is xm_{0} + ym'_{0} Â¶ xy_{0} with the following two Rules:-- (1) _Two Nullities, with Unlike Eliminands, yield a Nullity, in which both Retinends keep their Signs._ pg076 (2) _A Retinend, asserted in the Premisses to exist, may be so asserted in the Conclusion._ [Note that Rule (1) is merely the Formula expressed in words.] Fig </s>
<s> II </s>
<s> This includes any Pair of Premisses, of which one is a Nullity and the other an Entity, and which contain Like Eliminands </s>
<s> The simplest case is xm_{0} + ym_{1} Â·---------------Â· Â·-------Â· | | | | | | | Â·---|---Â· | |---|---| | |(O)|(O)| | |(I)| | |---|---|---|---| Â·-------Â· | |(I)| | | | Â·---|---Â· | '. </s>
<s> x'y_{1} | | | Â·---------------Â· In this case we see that the Conclusion is an Entity, and that the Nullity-Retinend has changed its Sign </s>
<s> And we should find this Rule to hold good with _any_ Pair of Premisses which fulfil the given conditions </s>
<s> [The Reader had better satisfy himself of this, by working out, on Diagrams, several varieties, such as x'm_{0} + ym_{1} (which Â¶ xy_{1}) x_{1}m'_{0} + y'm'_{1} (which Â¶ x'y'_{1}) m_{1}x_{0} + y'm_{1} (which Â¶ x'y'_{1}).] The Formula, to be remembered, is, xm_{0} + ym_{1} Â¶ x'y_{1} with the following Rule:-- _A Nullity and an Entity, with Like Eliminands, yield an Entity, in which the Nullity-Retinend changes its Sign._ [Note that this Rule is merely the Formula expressed in words.] pg077 Fig </s>
<s> III </s>
<s> This includes any Pair of Premisses which are both of them Nullities, and which contain Like Eliminands asserted to exist </s>
<s> The simplest case is xm_{0} + ym_{0} + m_{1} [Note that "m_{1}" is here stated _separately_, because it does not matter in which of the two Premisses it occurs: so that this includes the _three_ forms "m_{1}x_{0} + ym_{0}", "xm_{0} + m_{1}y_{0}", and "m_{1}x_{0} + m_{1}y_{0}".] Â·---------------Â· Â·-------Â· | | | | | | | Â·---|---Â· | |---|---| | |(O)|(O)| | | |(I)| |---|---|---|---| Â·-------Â· | |(O)|(I)| | | Â·---|---Â· | '. </s>
<s> x'y'_{1} | | | Â·---------------Â· In this case we see that the Conclusion is an Entity, and that _both_ Retinends have changed their Signs </s>
<s> And we should find this Rule to hold good with _any_ Pair of Premisses which fulfil the given conditions </s>
<s> [The Reader had better satisfy himself of this, by working out, on Diagrams, several varieties, such as x'm_{0} + m_{1}y_{0} (which Â¶ xy'_{1}) m'_{1}x_{0} + m'y'_{0} (which Â¶ x'y_{1}) m_{1}x'_{0} + m_{1}y'_{0} (which Â¶ xy_{1}).] The Formula, to be remembered, is xm_{0} + ym_{0} + m_{1} Â¶ x'y'_{1} with the following Rule (which is merely the Formula expressed in words):-- _Two Nullities, with Like Eliminands asserted to exist, yield an Entity, in which both Retinends change their Signs._ * * * * * In order to help the Reader to remember the peculiarities and FormulÃ¦ of these three Figures, I will put them all together in one Table </s>

<s> _Fallacies._ Any argument which _deceives_ us, by seeming to prove what it does not really prove, may be called a '=Fallacy=' (derived from the Latin verb _fallo_ "I deceive"): but the particular kind, to be now discussed, consists of a Pair of Propositions, which are proposed as the Premisses of a Syllogism, but yield no Conclusion </s>
<s> When each of the proposed Premisses is a Proposition in _I_, or _E_, or _A_, (the only kinds with which we are now concerned,) the Fallacy may be detected by the 'Method of Diagrams,' by simply setting them out on a Triliteral Diagram, and observing that they yield no information which can be transferred to the Biliteral Diagram </s>
<s> But suppose we were working by the 'Method of _Subscripts_,' and had to deal with a Pair of proposed Premisses, which happened to be a 'Fallacy,' how could we be certain that they would not yield any Conclusion </s>
<s> Our best plan is, I think, to deal with _Fallacies_ in the same was as we have already dealt with _Syllogisms_: that is, to take certain forms of Pairs of Propositions, and to work them out, once for all, on the Triliteral Diagram, and ascertain that they yield _no_ Conclusion; and then to record them, for future use, as _FormulÃ¦ for Fallacies_, just as we have already recorded our three _FormulÃ¦ for Syllogisms_ </s>
<s> pg082 Now, if we were to record the two Sets of FormulÃ¦ in the _same_ shape, viz </s>
<s> by the Method of Subscripts, there would be considerable risk of confusing the two kinds </s>
<s> Hence, in order to keep them distinct, I propose to record the FormulÃ¦ for _Fallacies_ in _words_, and to call them "Forms" instead of "FormulÃ¦" </s>
<s> Let us now proceed to find, by the Method of Diagrams, three "Forms of Fallacies," which we will then put on record for future use </s>
<s> They are as follows:-- (1) Fallacy of Like Eliminands not asserted to exist </s>
<s> (2) Fallacy of Unlike Eliminands with an Entity-Premiss </s>
<s> (3) Fallacy of two Entity-Premisses </s>
<s> These shall be discussed separately, and it will be seen that each fails to yield a Conclusion </s>
<s> (1) _Fallacy of Like Eliminands not asserted to exist._ It is evident that neither of the given Propositions can be an _Entity_, since that kind asserts the _existence_ of both of its Terms (see p </s>
<s> 20) </s>
<s> Hence they must both be _Nullities_ </s>
<s> Hence the given Pair may be represented by (xm_{0} + ym_{0}), with or without x_{1}, y_{1} </s>
<s> These, set out on Triliteral Diagrams, are xm_{0} + ym_{0} x_{1}m_{0} + ym_{0} Â·---------------Â· Â·---------------Â· | | | | (I) | | Â·---|---Â· | | Â·---|---Â· | | |(O)|(O)| | | |(O)|(O)| | |---|---|---|---| |---|---|---|---| | |(O)| | | | |(O)| | | | Â·---|---Â· | | Â·---|---Â· | | | | | | | Â·---------------Â· Â·---------------Â· xm_{0} + y_{1}m_{0} x_{1}m_{0} + y_{1}m_{0} Â·---------------Â· Â·---------------Â· | | | | (I) | | Â·---|---Â· | | Â·---|---Â· | | |(O)|(O)| | | |(O)|(O)| | |(I)|---|---|---| |(I)|---|---|---| | |(O)| | | | |(O)| | | | Â·---|---Â· | | Â·---|---Â· | | | | | | | Â·---------------Â· Â·---------------Â· pg083 (2) _Fallacy of Unlike Eliminands with an Entity-Premiss._ Here the given Pair may be represented by (xm_{0} + ym'_{1}) with or without x_{1} or m_{1} </s>
<s> These, set out on Triliteral Diagrams, are xm_{0} + ym'_{1} x_{1}m_{0} + ym'_{1} m_{1}x_{0} + ym'_{1} Â·---------------Â· Â·---------------Â· Â·---------------Â· | | | | (I) | | | | | Â·---|---Â· | | Â·---|---Â· | | Â·---|---Â· | | |(O)|(O)| | | |(O)|(O)| | | |(O)|(O)| | |(I)|---|---|---| |(I)|---|---|---| |(I)|---|---|---| | | | | | | | | | | | | (I) | | | Â·---|---Â· | | Â·---|---Â· | | Â·---|---Â· | | | | | | | | | | Â·---------------Â· Â·---------------Â· Â·---------------Â· (3) _Fallacy of two Entity-Premisses._ Here the given Pair may be represented by either (xm_{1} + ym_{1}) or (xm_{1} + ym'_{1}) </s>
<s> These, set out on Triliteral Diagrams, are xm_{1} + ym_{1} xm_{1} + ym'_{1} Â·---------------Â· Â·---------------Â· | | | | | | | Â·---|---Â· | | Â·---|---Â· | | | (I) | | | | (I) | | |---|(I)|---|---| |(I)|---|---|---| | | | | | | | | | | | Â·---|---Â· | | Â·---|---Â· | | | | | | | Â·---------------Â· Â·---------------Â· pg084 Â§ 4 </s>
<s> _Method of proceeding with a given Pair of Propositions._ Let us suppose that we have before us a Pair of Propositions of Relation, which contain between them a Pair of codivisional Classes, and that we wish to ascertain what Conclusion, if any, is consequent from them </s>
<s> We translate them, if necessary, into subscript-form, and then proceed as follows:-- (1) We examine their Subscripts, in order to see whether they are (a) a Pair of Nullities; or (b) a Nullity and an Entity; or (c) a Pair of Entities </s>
<s> (2) If they are a Pair of Nullities, we examine their Eliminands, in order to see whether they are Unlike or Like </s>
<s> If their Eliminands are _Unlike_, it is a case of Fig </s>
<s> I </s>
<s> We then examine their Retinends, to see whether one or both of them are asserted to _exist_ </s>
<s> If one Retinend is so asserted, it is a case of Fig </s>
<s> I (a); if both, it is a case of Fig </s>
<s> I (b) </s>
<s> If their Eliminands are Like, we examine them, in order to see whether either of them is asserted to exist </s>
<s> If so, it is a case of Fig </s>
<s> III.; if not, it is a case of "Fallacy of Like Eliminands not asserted to exist" </s>
<s> (3) If they are a Nullity and an Entity, we examine their Eliminands, in order to see whether they are Like or Unlike </s>
<s> If their Eliminands are Like, it is a case of Fig </s>
<s> II.; if _Unlike_, it is a case of "Fallacy of Unlike Eliminands with an Entity-Premiss" </s>
<s> (4) If they are a Pair of Entities, it is a case of "Fallacy of two Entity-Premisses" </s>

<s> 100); Â§ =5=, 1-12 (p </s>
<s> 101); Â§ =6=, 7-12 (p </s>
<s> 106); Â§ =7=, 7-12 (p </s>
<s> 108).] pg085 BOOK VII </s>
<s> SORITESES </s>
<s> CHAPTER I </s>
<s> _INTRODUCTORY._ When a Set of three or more Biliteral Propositions are such that all their Terms are Species of the same Genus, and are also so related that two of them, taken together, yield a Conclusion, which, taken with another of them, yields another Conclusion, and so on, until all have been taken, it is evident that, if the original Set were true, the last Conclusion would _also_ be true </s>
<s> Such a Set, with the last Conclusion tacked on, is called a '=Sorites='; the original Set of Propositions is called its '=Premisses='; each of the intermediate Conclusions is called a '=Partial Conclusion=' of the Sorites; the last Conclusion is called its '=Complete Conclusion=,' or, more briefly, its '=Conclusion='; the Genus, of which all the Terms are Species, is called its '=Universe of Discourse=', or, more briefly, its '=Univ.='; the Terms, used as Eliminands in the Syllogisms, are called its '=Eliminands='; and the two Terms, which are retained, and therefore appear in the Conclusion, are called its '=Retinends=' </s>
<s> [Note that each _Partial_ Conclusion contains one or two _Eliminands_; but that the _Complete_ Conclusion contains _Retinends_ only.] The Conclusion is said to be '=consequent=' from the Premisses; for which reason it is usual to prefix to it the word "Therefore" (or the symbol "'.".) </s>
<s> [Note that the question, whether the Conclusion is or is not _consequent_ from the Premisses, is not affected by the _actual_ truth or falsity of any one of the Propositions which make up the Sorites, by depends entirely on their _relationship to one another_ </s>
<s> pg086 As a specimen-Sorites, let us take the following Set of 5 Propositions:-- (1) "No a are b'; (2) All b are c; (3) All c are d; (4) No e' are a'; (5) All h are e'" </s>
<s> Here the first and second, taken together, yield "No a are c'" </s>
<s> This, taken along with the third, yields "No a are d'" </s>
<s> This, taken along with the fourth, yields "No d' are e'" </s>
<s> And this, taken along with the fifth, yields "All h are d" </s>
<s> Hence, if the original Set were true, this would _also_ be true </s>
<s> Hence the original Set, with this tacked on, is a _Sorites_; the original Set is its _Premisses_; the Proposition "All h are d" is its _Conclusion_; the Terms a, b, c, e are its _Eliminands_; and the Terms d and h are its _Retinends_ </s>
<s> Hence we may write the whole Sorites thus:-- "No a are b'; All b are c; All c are d; No e' are a'; All h are e' </s>
<s> '. </s>
<s> All h are d" </s>
<s> In the above Sorites, the 3 Partial Conclusions are the Positions "No a are e'", "No a are d'", "No d' are e'"; but, if the Premisses were arranged in other ways, other Partial Conclusions might be obtained </s>
<s> Thus, the order 41523 yields the Partial Conclusions "No c' are b'", "All h are b", "All h are c" </s>
<s> There are altogether _nine_ Partial Conclusions to this Sorites, which the Reader will find it an interesting task to make out for himself.] pg087 CHAPTER II </s>
<s> _PROBLEMS IN SORITESES._ Â§ 1 </s>
<s> _Introductory._ The Problems we shall have to solve are of the following form:-- "Given three or more Propositions of Relation, which are proposed as Premisses: to ascertain what Conclusion, if any, is consequent from them" </s>
<s> We will limit ourselves, at present, to Problems which can be worked by the FormulÃ¦ of Fig </s>
<s> I </s>
<s> (See p </s>
<s> 75.) Those, that require _other_ FormulÃ¦, are rather too hard for beginners </s>
<s> Such Problems may be solved by either of two Methods, viz </s>
<s> (1) The Method of Separate Syllogisms; (2) The Method of Underscoring </s>
<s> These shall be discussed separately </s>
<s> pg088 Â§ 2 </s>
<s> _Solution by Method of Separate Syllogisms._ The Rules, for doing this, are as follows:-- (1) Name the 'Universe of Discourse' </s>
<s> (2) Construct a Dictionary, making a, b, c, &c </s>
<s> represent the Terms </s>
<s> (3) Put the Proposed Premisses into subscript form </s>
<s> (4) Select two which, containing between them a pair of codivisional Classes, can be used as the Premisses of a Syllogism </s>
<s> (5) Find their Conclusion by Formula </s>
<s> (6) Find a third Premiss which, along with this Conclusion, can be used as the Premisses of a second Syllogism </s>
<s> (7) Find a second Conclusion by Formula </s>
<s> (8) Proceed thus, until all the proposed Premisses have been used </s>
<s> (9) Put the last Conclusion, which is the Complete Conclusion of the Sorites, into concrete form </s>
<s> [As an example of this process, let us take, as the proposed Set of Premisses, (1) "All the policemen on this beat sup with our cook; (2) No man with long hair can fail to be a poet; (3) Amos Judd has never been in prison; (4) Our cook's 'cousins' all love cold mutton; (5) None but policemen on this beat are poets; (6) None but her 'cousins' ever sup with our cook; (7) Men with short hair have all been in prison" </s>

<s> _Solution by Method of Underscoring._ Consider the Pair of Premisses xm_{0} + ym'_{0} which yield the Conclusion xy_{0} We see that, in order to get this Conclusion, we must eliminate m and m', and write x and y together in one expression </s>
<s> Now, if we agree to _mark_ m and m' as eliminated, and to read the two expressions together, as if they were written in one, the two Premisses will then exactly represent the _Conclusion_, and we need not write it out separately </s>
<s> Let us agree to mark the eliminated letters by _underscoring_ them, putting a _single_ score under the _first_, and a _double_ one under the _second_ </s>
<s> The two Premisses now become xm_{0} + ym'_{0} - = which we read as "xy_{0}" </s>
<s> In copying out the Premisses for underscoring, it will be convenient to _omit all subscripts_ </s>
<s> As to the "0's" we may always _suppose_ them written, and, as to the "1's", we are not concerned to know _which_ Terms are asserted to _exist_, except those which appear in the _Complete_ Conclusion; and for _them_ it will be easy enough to refer to the original list </s>
<s> pg092 [I will now go through the process of solving, by this method, the example worked in Â§ 2 </s>

<s> [N.B </s>
<s> In each Example, in Sections 8 and 9, it is possible to begin with _any_ Premiss, at pleasure, and thus to get as many different Solutions (all of course yielding the _same_ Complete Conclusion) as there are Premisses in the Example </s>
<s> Hence Â§ 8 really contains 129 different Examples, and Â§ 9 contains 273.] pg112 Â§ 9 </s>

<s> pg134 CHAPTER III </s>
<s> _SOLUTIONS._ Â§ 1 </s>
<s> _Propositions of Relation reduced to normal form._ _Solutions for Â§ 1._ SL1 1 </s>
<s> The Univ </s>
<s> is "persons" </s>
<s> The Individual "I" may be regarded as a Class, of persons, whose peculiar Attribute is "represented by the Name 'I'", and may be called the Class of "I's" </s>
<s> It is evident that this Class cannot possibly contain more than one Member: hence the Sign of Quantity is "all" </s>
<s> The verb "have been" may be replaced by the phrase "are persons who have been" </s>
<s> The Proposition may be written thus:-- "All" _Sign of Quantity_ </s>
<s> "I's" _Subject_ </s>
<s> "are" _Copula_ </s>
<s> "persons who have been out for a walk" _Predicate_ </s>
<s> or, more briefly, "All | I's | are | persons who have been out for a walk" </s>
<s> 2 </s>
<s> The Univ </s>
<s> and the Subject are the same as in Ex </s>
<s> 1 </s>
<s> The Proposition may be written "All | I's | are | persons who feel better" </s>
<s> 3 </s>
<s> Univ </s>
<s> is "persons" </s>
<s> The Subject is evidently the Class of persons from which John is _excluded_; _i.e._ it is the Class containing all persons who are _not_ "John" </s>
<s> The Sign of Quantity is "no" </s>
<s> The verb "has read" may be replaced by the phrase "are persons who have read" </s>
<s> The Proposition may be written "No | persons who are not 'John' | are | persons who have read the letter" </s>
<s> 4 </s>
<s> Univ </s>
<s> is "persons" </s>
<s> The Subject is evidently the Class of persons whose only two Members are "you and I" </s>
<s> Hence the Sign of Quantity is "no" </s>
<s> The Proposition may be written "No | Members of the Class 'you and I' | are | old persons" </s>
<s> pg135 5 </s>
<s> Univ </s>
<s> is "creatures" </s>
<s> The verb "run well" may be replaced by the phrase "are creatures that run well" </s>
<s> The Proposition may be written "No | fat creatures | are | creatures that run well" </s>
<s> 6 </s>
<s> Univ </s>
<s> is "persons" </s>
<s> The Subject is evidently the Class of persons who are _not_ brave </s>
<s> The verb "deserve" may be replaced by the phrase "are deserving of" </s>
<s> The Proposition may be written "No | not-brave persons | are | persons deserving of the fair" </s>
<s> 7 </s>
<s> Univ </s>
<s> is "persons" </s>
<s> The phrase "looks poetical" evidently belongs to the _Predicate_; and the _Subject_ is the Class, of persons, whose peculiar Attribute is "_not_-pale" </s>
<s> The Proposition may be written "No | not-pale persons | are | persons who look poetical" </s>
<s> 8 </s>
<s> Univ </s>
<s> is "persons" </s>
<s> The Proposition may be written "Some | judges | are | persons who lose their tempers" </s>
<s> 9 </s>
<s> Univ </s>
<s> is "persons" </s>
<s> The phrase "never neglect" is merely a stronger form of the phrase "am a person who does not neglect" </s>
<s> The Proposition may be written "All | 'I's' | are | persons who do not neglect important business" </s>
<s> 10 </s>
<s> Univ </s>
<s> is "things" </s>
<s> The phrase "what is difficult" (_i.e._ "that which is difficult") is equivalent to the phrase "all difficult things" </s>
<s> The Proposition may be written "All | difficult things | are | things that need attention" </s>
<s> 11 </s>
<s> Univ </s>
<s> is "things" </s>
<s> The phrase "what is unwholesome" may be interpreted as in Ex </s>
<s> 10 </s>
<s> The Proposition may be written "All | unwholesome things | are | things that should be avoided" </s>
<s> 12 </s>
<s> Univ </s>
<s> is "laws" </s>
<s> The Predicate is evidently a Class whose peculiar Attribute is "relating to excise" </s>
<s> The Proposition may be written "All | laws passed last week | are | laws relating to excise" </s>
<s> 13 </s>
<s> Univ </s>
<s> is "things" </s>
<s> The Subject is evidently the Class, of studies, whose peculiar Attribute is "logical"; hence the Sign of Quantity is "all" </s>
<s> The Proposition may be written "All | logical studies | are | things that puzzle me" </s>
<s> 14 </s>
<s> Univ </s>
<s> is "persons" </s>

<s> The Proposition may be written "No | persons in the house | are | Jews" </s>
<s> 15 </s>
<s> Univ </s>
<s> is "dishes" </s>
<s> The phrase "if not well-cooked" is equivalent to the Attribute "not well-cooked" </s>
<s> The Proposition may be written "Some | not well-cooked dishes | are | unwholesome dishes" </s>
<s> pg136 16 </s>
<s> Univ </s>
<s> is "books" </s>
<s> The phrase "make one drowsy" may be replaced by the phrase "are books that make one drowsy" </s>
<s> The Sign of Quantity is evidently "all" </s>
<s> The Proposition may be written "All | unexciting books | are | books that make one drowsy" </s>
<s> 17 </s>
<s> Univ </s>
<s> is "men" </s>
<s> The Subject is evidently "a man who knows what he's about"; and the word "when" shows that the Proposition is asserted of _every_ such man, _i.e._ of _all_ such men </s>
<s> The verb "can" may be replaced by "are men who can" </s>
<s> The Proposition may be written "All | men who know what they're about | are | men who can detect a sharper" </s>
<s> 18 </s>
<s> The Univ </s>
<s> and the Subject are the same as in Ex </s>
<s> 4 </s>

<s> 19 </s>
<s> Univ </s>
<s> is "persons" </s>
<s> The verb "wear" may be replaced by the phrase "are accustomed to wear" </s>
<s> The Proposition may be written "Some | bald persons | are | persons accustomed to wear wigs" </s>
<s> 20 </s>
<s> Univ </s>
<s> is "persons" </s>
<s> The phrase "never talk" is merely a stronger form of "are persons who do not talk" </s>
<s> The Proposition may be written "All | fully occupied persons | are | persons who do not talk about their grievances" </s>
<s> 21 </s>
<s> Univ </s>
<s> is "riddles" </s>
<s> The phrase "if they can be solved" is equivalent to the Attribute "that can be solved" </s>
<s> The Proposition may be written "No | riddles that can be solved | are | riddles that interest me" </s>

<s> pg164 NOTES </s>
<s> (A) [See p </s>
<s> 80] </s>
<s> One of the favourite objections, brought against the Science of Logic by its detractors, is that a Syllogism has no real validity as an argument, since it involves the Fallacy of _Petitio Principii_ (i.e </s>
<s> "Begging the Question", the essence of which is that the whole Conclusion is involved in _one_ of the Premisses) </s>
<s> This formidable objection is refuted, with beautiful clearness and simplicity, by these three Diagrams, which show us that, in each of the three Figures, the Conclusion is really involved in the _two_ Premisses taken together, each contributing its share </s>
<s> Thus, in Fig </s>
<s> I., the Premiss xm_{0} empties the _Inner_ Cell of the N.W </s>
<s> Quarter, while the Premiss ym_{0} empties its _Outer_ Cell </s>
<s> Hence it needs the _two_ Premisses to empty the _whole_ of the N.W </s>
<s> Quarter, and thus to prove the Conclusion xy_{0} </s>
<s> Again, in Fig </s>
<s> II., the Premiss xm_{0} empties the Inner Cell of the N.W </s>
<s> Quarter </s>
<s> The Premiss ym_{1} merely tells us that the Inner Portion of the W </s>
<s> Half is _occupied_, so that we may place a 'I' in it, _somewhere_; but, if this were the _whole_ of our information, we should not know in _which_ Cell to place it, so that it would have to 'sit on the fence': it is only when we learn, from the other Premiss, that the _upper_ of these two Cells is _empty_, that we feel authorised to place the 'I' in the _lower_ Cell, and thus to prove the Conclusion x'y_{1} </s>
<s> Lastly, in Fig </s>
<s> III., the information, that m _exists_, merely authorises us to place a 'I' _somewhere_ in the Inner Square----but it has large choice of fences to sit upon </s>
<s> It needs the Premiss xm_{0} to drive it out of the N </s>
<s> Half of that Square; and it needs the Premiss ym_{0} to drive it out of the W </s>
<s> Half </s>
<s> Hence it needs the _two_ Premisses to drive it into the Inner Portion of the S.E </s>
<s> Quarter, and thus to prove the Conclusion x'y'_{1} </s>
<s> pg165 APPENDIX, ADDRESSED TO TEACHERS </s>
<s> Â§ 1 </s>
<s> _Introductory._ There are several matters, too hard to discuss with _Learners_, which nevertheless need to be explained to any _Teachers_, into whose hands this book may fall, in order that they may thoroughly understand what my Symbolic Method _is_, and in what respects it differs from the many other Methods already published </s>
<s> These matters are as follows:-- The "Existential Import" of Propositions </s>
<s> The use of "is-not" (or "are-not") as a Copula </s>
<s> The theory "two Negative Premisses prove nothing" </s>
<s> Euler's Method of Diagrams </s>
<s> Venn's Method of Diagrams </s>
<s> My Method of Diagrams </s>
<s> The Solution of a Syllogism by various Methods </s>
<s> My Method of treating Syllogisms and Sorites </s>
<s> Some account of Parts II, III </s>
<s> Â§ 2 </s>
<s> _The "Existential Import" of Propositions._ The writers, and editors, of the Logical text-books which run in the ordinary grooves----to whom I shall hereafter refer by the (I hope inoffensive) title "The Logicians"----take, on this subject, what seems to me to be a more humble position than is at all necessary </s>
<s> They speak of the Copula of a Proposition "with bated breath", almost as if it were a living, conscious Entity, capable of declaring for itself what it chose to mean, and that we, poor human creatures, had nothing to do but to ascertain _what_ was its sovereign will and pleasure, and submit to it </s>
<s> pg166 In opposition to this view, I maintain that any writer of a book is fully authorised in attaching any meaning he likes to any word or phrase he intends to use </s>
<s> If I find an author saying, at the beginning of his book, "Let it be understood that by the word '_black_' I shall always mean '_white_', and that by the word '_white_' I shall always mean '_black_'," I meekly accept his ruling, however injudicious I may think it </s>
<s> And so, with regard to the question whether a Proposition is or is not to be understood as asserting the existence of its Subject, I maintain that every writer may adopt his own rule, provided of course that it is consistent with itself and with the accepted facts of Logic </s>
<s> Let us consider certain views that may _logically_ be held, and thus settle which of them may _conveniently_ be held; after which I shall hold myself free to declare which of them _I_ intend to hold </s>
<s> The _kinds_ of Propositions, to be considered, are those that begin with "some", with "no", and with "all" </s>
<s> These are usually called Propositions "in _I_", "in _E_", and "in _A_" </s>
<s> First, then, a Proposition in _I_ may be understood as asserting, or else as _not_ asserting, the existence of its Subject </s>
<s> (By "existence" I mean of course whatever kind of existence suits its nature </s>
<s> The two Propositions, "_dreams_ exist" and "_drums_ exist", denote two totally different kinds of "existence" </s>
<s> A _dream_ is an aggregate of ideas, and exists only in the _mind of a dreamer_: whereas a _drum_ is an aggregate of wood and parchment, and exists in _the hands of a drummer_.) First, let us suppose that _I_ "asserts" (i.e </s>
<s> "asserts the existence of its Subject") </s>
<s> Here, of course, we must regard a Proposition in _A_ as making the _same_ assertion, since it necessarily _contains_ a Proposition in _I_ </s>
<s> We now have _I_ and _A_ "asserting" </s>
<s> Does this leave us free to make what supposition we choose as to _E_ </s>
<s> My answer is "No </s>
<s> We are tied down to the supposition that _E_ does _not_ assert" </s>
<s> This can be proved as follows:-- If possible, let _E_ "assert" </s>
<s> Then (taking x, y, and z to represent Attributes) we see that, if the Proposition "No xy are z" be true, some things exist with the Attributes x and y: i.e </s>
<s> "Some x are y" </s>
<s> pg167 Also we know that, if the Proposition "Some xy are z" be true, the same result follows </s>
<s> But these two Propositions are Contradictories, so that one or other of them _must_ be true </s>
<s> Hence this result is _always_ true: i.e </s>
<s> the Proposition "Some x are y" is _always_ true </s>
<s> _Quod est absurdum._ (See Note (A), p </s>
<s> 195) </s>
<s> We see, then, that the supposition "_I_ asserts" necessarily leads to "_A_ asserts, but _E_ does not" </s>
<s> And this is the _first_ of the various views that may conceivably be held </s>
<s> Next, let us suppose that _I_ does _not_ "assert" </s>
<s> And, along with this, let us take the supposition that _E_ _does_ "assert" </s>
<s> Hence the Proposition "No x are y" means "Some x exist, and none of them are y": i.e </s>
<s> "_all_ of them are _not_-y," which is a Proposition in _A_ </s>
<s> We also know, of course, that the Proposition "All x are not-y" proves "No x are y" </s>
<s> Now two Propositions, each of which proves the other, are _equivalent_ </s>
<s> Hence every Proposition in _A_ is equivalent to one in _E_, and therefore "_asserts_" </s>
<s> Hence our _second_ conceivable view is "_E_ and _A_ assert, but _I_ does not" </s>
<s> This view does not seen to involve any necessary contradiction with itself or with the accepted facts of Logic </s>
<s> But, when we come to _test_ it, as applied to the actual _facts_ of life, we shall find I think, that it fits in with them so badly that its adoption would be, to say the least of it, singularly inconvenient for ordinary folk </s>
<s> Let me record a little dialogue I have just held with my friend Jones, who is trying to form a new Club, to be regulated on strictly _Logical_ principles </s>
<s> _Author._ "Well, Jones </s>
<s> Have you got your new Club started yet" </s>
<s> _Jones_ (_rubbing his hands_) </s>
<s> "You'll be glad to hear that some of the Members (mind, I only say '_some_') are millionaires </s>
<s> Rolling in gold, my boy" </s>
<s> _Author._ "That sounds well </s>
<s> And how many Members have entered" </s>
<s> _Jones_ (_staring_) </s>
<s> "None at all </s>
<s> We haven't got it started yet </s>
<s> What makes you think we have" </s>
<s> _Author._ "Why, I thought you said that some of the Members----" pg168 _Jones_ (_contemptuously_) </s>
<s> "You don't seem to be aware that we're working on strictly _Logical_ principles </s>
<s> A _Particular_ Proposition does _not_ assert the existence of its Subject </s>
<s> I merely meant to say that we've made a Rule not to admit _any_ Members till we have at least _three_ Candidates whose incomes are over ten thousand a year" </s>
<s> _Author._ "Oh, _that's_ what you meant, is it </s>
<s> Let's hear some more of your Rules" </s>
<s> _Jones._ "Another is, that no one, who has been convicted seven times of forgery, is admissible" </s>
<s> _Author._ "And here, again, I suppose you don't mean to assert there _are_ any such convicts in existence" </s>
<s> _Jones._ "Why, that's exactly what I _do_ mean to assert </s>
<s> Don't you know that a Universal Negative _asserts_ the existence of its Subject </s>
<s> _Of course_ we didn't make that Rule till we had satisfied ourselves that there are several such convicts now living" </s>
<s> The Reader can now decide for himself how far this _second_ conceivable view would fit in with the facts of life </s>
<s> He will, I think, agree with me that Jones' view, of the 'Existential Import' of Propositions, would lead to some inconvenience </s>
<s> Thirdly, let us suppose that neither _I_ nor _E_ "asserts" </s>
<s> Now the supposition that the two Propositions, "Some x are y" and "No x are not-y", do _not_ "assert", necessarily involves the supposition that "All x are y" does _not_ "assert", since it would be absurd to suppose that they assert, when combined, more than they do when taken separately </s>
<s> Hence the _third_ (and last) of the conceivable views is that neither _I_, nor _E_, nor _A_, "asserts" </s>
<s> The advocates of this third view would interpret the Proposition "Some x are y" to mean "If there _were_ any x in existence, some of them _would_ be y"; and so with _E_ and _A_ </s>
<s> It admits of proof that this view, as regards _A_, conflicts with the accepted facts of Logic </s>
<s> Let us take the Syllogism _Darapti_, which is universally accepted as valid </s>
<s> Its form is "All m are x; All m are y </s>
<s> '. </s>
<s> Some y are x" </s>
<s> pg169 This they would interpret as follows:-- "If there were any m in existence, all of them would be x; If there were any m in existence, all of them would be y </s>
<s> '. </s>
<s> If there were any y in existence, some of them would be x" </s>
<s> That this Conclusion does _not_ follow has been so briefly and clearly explained by Mr Keynes (in his "Formal Logic", dated 1894, pp </s>
<s> 356, 357), that I prefer to quote his words:-- "_Let no proposition imply the existence either of its subject or of its predicate._ "Take, as an example, a syllogism in _Darapti_:-- '_All M is P_, _All M is S_, _'. </s>
<s> Some S is P_' </s>
<s> "Taking S, M, P, as the minor, middle, and major terms respectively, the conclusion will imply that, if there is an S, there is some P </s>
<s> Will the premisses also imply this </s>
<s> If so, then the syllogism is valid; but not otherwise </s>
<s> "The conclusion implies that if S exists P exists; but, consistently with the premisses, S may be existent while M and P are both non-existent </s>
<s> An implication is, therefore, contained in the conclusion, which is not justified by the premisses" </s>
<s> This seems to _me_ entirely clear and convincing </s>
<s> Still, "to make sicker", I may as well throw the above (_soi-disant_) Syllogism into a concrete form, which will be within the grasp of even a _non_-logical Reader </s>
<s> Let us suppose that a Boys' School has been set up, with the following system of Rules:-- "All boys in the First (the highest) Class are to do French, Greek, and Latin </s>
<s> All in the Second Class are to do Greek only </s>
<s> All in the Third Class are to do Latin only" </s>
<s> Suppose also that there _are_ boys in the Third Class, and in the Second; but that no boy has yet risen into the First </s>
<s> It is evident that there are no boys in the School doing French: still we know, by the Rules, what would happen if there _were_ any </s>
<s> pg170 We are authorised, then, by the _Data_, to assert the following two Propositions:-- "If there were any boys doing French, all of them would be doing Greek; If there were any boys doing French, all of them would be doing Latin" </s>
<s> And the Conclusion, according to "The Logicians" would be "If there were any boys doing Latin, some of them would be doing Greek" </s>
<s> Here, then, we have two _true_ Premisses and a _false_ Conclusion (since we know that there _are_ boys doing Latin, and that _none_ of them are doing Greek) </s>
<s> Hence the argument is _invalid_ </s>
<s> Similarly it may be shown that this "non-existential" interpretation destroys the validity of _Disamis_, _Datisi_, _Felapton_, and _Fresison_ </s>
<s> Some of "The Logicians" will, no doubt, be ready to reply "But we are not _Aldrichians_ </s>
<s> Why should _we_ be responsible for the validity of the Syllogisms of so antiquated an author as Aldrich" </s>
<s> Very good </s>
<s> Then, for the _special_ benefit of these "friends" of mine (with what ominous emphasis that name is sometimes used </s>
<s> "I must have a private interview with _you_, my young _friend_," says the bland Dr </s>
<s> Birch, "in my library, at 9 a.m </s>
<s> tomorrow </s>
<s> And you will please to be _punctual_"!), for their _special_ benefit, I say, I will produce _another_ charge against this "non-existential" interpretation </s>
<s> It actually invalidates the ordinary Process of "Conversion", as applied to Proposition in '_I_' </s>
<s> _Every_ logician, Aldrichian or otherwise, accepts it as an established fact that "Some x are y" may be legitimately converted into "Some y are x" </s>
<s> But is it equally clear that the Proposition "If there _were_ any x, some of them _would_ be y" may be legitimately converted into "If there _were_ any y, some of them would be x" </s>
<s> I trow not </s>
<s> The example I have already used----of a Boys' School with a non-existent First Class----will serve admirably to illustrate this new flaw in the theory of "The Logicians" </s>
<s> pg171 Let us suppose that there is yet _another_ Rule in this School, viz </s>
<s> "In each Class, at the end of the Term, the head boy and the second boy shall receive prizes" </s>
<s> This Rule entirely authorises us to assert (in the sense in which "The Logicians" would use the words) "Some boys in the First Class will receive prizes", for this simply means (according to them) "If there _were_ any boys in the First Class, some of them _would_ receive prizes" </s>
<s> Now the Converse of this Proposition is, of course, "Some boys, who will receive prizes, are in the First Class", which means (according to "The Logicians") "If there _were_ any boys about to receive prizes, some of them _would_ be in the First Class" (which Class we know to be _empty_) </s>
<s> Of this Pair of Converse Propositions, the first is undoubtedly _true_: the second, _as_ undoubtedly, _false_ </s>
<s> It is always sad to see a batsman knock down his own wicket: one pities him, as a man and a brother, but, as a _cricketer_, one can but pronounce him "Out" </s>
<s> We see, then, that, among all the conceivable views we have here considered, there are only _two_ which can _logically_ be held, viz </s>
<s> _I_ and _A_ "assert", but _E_ does not </s>
<s> _E_ and _A_ "assert", but _I_ does not </s>
<s> The _second_ of these I have shown to involve great practical inconvenience </s>
<s> The _first_ is the one adopted in this book </s>
<s> (See p </s>
<s> 19.) Some further remarks on this subject will be found in Note (B), at p </s>
<s> 196 </s>
<s> Â§ 3 </s>
<s> _The use of "is-not" (or "are-not") as a Copula._ Is it better to say "John _is-not_ in-the-house" or "John _is_ not-in-the-house" </s>
<s> "Some of my acquaintances _are-not_ men-I-should-like-to-be-seen-with" or "Some of my acquaintances _are_ men-I-should-_not_-like-to-be-seen-with" </s>
<s> That is the sort of question we have now to discuss </s>
<s> pg172 This is no question of Logical Right and Wrong: it is merely a matter of _taste_, since the two forms mean exactly the same thing </s>
<s> And here, again, "The Logicians" seem to me to take much too humble a position </s>
<s> When they are putting the final touches to the grouping of their Proposition, just before the curtain goes up, and when the Copula----always a rather fussy 'heavy father', asks them "Am _I_ to have the 'not', or will you tack it on to the Predicate" </s>
<s> they are much too ready to answer, like the subtle cab-driver, "Leave it to _you_, Sir" </s>
<s> The result seems to be, that the grasping Copula constantly gets a "not" that had better have been merged in the Predicate, and that Propositions are differentiated which had better have been recognised as precisely similar </s>
<s> Surely it is simpler to treat "Some men are Jews" and "Some men are Gentiles" as being both of them, _affirmative_ Propositions, instead of translating the latter into "Some men are-not Jews", and regarding it as a _negative_ Propositions </s>
<s> The fact is, "The Logicians" have somehow acquired a perfectly _morbid_ dread of negative Attributes, which makes them shut their eyes, like frightened children, when they come across such terrible Propositions as "All not-x are y"; and thus they exclude from their system many very useful forms of Syllogisms </s>
<s> Under the influence of this unreasoning terror, they plead that, in Dichotomy by Contradiction, the _negative_ part is too large to deal with, so that it is better to regard each Thing as either included in, or excluded from, the _positive_ part </s>
<s> I see no force in this plea: and the facts often go the other way </s>
<s> As a personal question, dear Reader, if _you_ were to group your acquaintances into the two Classes, men that you _would_ like to be seen with, and men that you would _not_ like to be seen with, do you think the latter group would be so _very_ much the larger of the two </s>
<s> For the purposes of Symbolic Logic, it is so _much_ the most convenient plan to regard the two sub-divisions, produced by Dichotomy, on the _same_ footing, and to say, of any Thing, either that it "is" in the one, or that it "is" in the other, that I do not think any Reader of this book is likely to demur to my adopting that course </s>
<s> pg173 Â§ 4 </s>
<s> _The theory that "two Negative Premisses prove nothing"._ This I consider to be _another_ craze of "The Logicians", fully as morbid as their dread of a negative Attribute </s>
<s> It is, perhaps, best refuted by the method of _Instantia Contraria_ </s>
<s> Take the following Pairs of Premisses:-- "None of my boys are conceited; None of my girls are greedy" </s>
<s> "None of my boys are clever; None but a clever boy could solve this problem" </s>
<s> "None of my boys are learned; Some of my boys are not choristers" </s>
<s> (This last Proposition is, in _my_ system, an _affirmative_ one, since I should read it "are not-choristers"; but, in dealing with "The Logicians," I may fairly treat it as a _negative_ one, since _they_ would read it "are-not choristers".) If you, dear Reader, declare, after full consideration of these Pairs of Premisses, that you cannot deduce a Conclusion from _any_ of them----why, all I can say is that, like the Duke in Patience, you "will have to be contented with our heart-felt sympathy" </s>
<s> [See Note (C), p </s>
<s> 196.] Â§ 5 </s>
<s> _Euler's Method of Diagrams._ Diagrams seem to have been used, at first, to represent _Propositions_ only </s>
<s> In Euler's well-known Circles, each was supposed to contain a class, and the Diagram consisted of two circles, which exhibited the relations, as to inclusion and exclusion, existing between the two Classes </s>
<s> _____ _/ ___ \_ / / y \ \ | \___/ | \_ x _/ \_____/ Thus, the Diagram, here given, exhibits the two Classes, whose respective Attributes are x and y, as so related to each other that the following Propositions are all simultaneously true:--"All x are y", "No x are not-y", "Some x are y", "Some y are not-x", "Some not-y are not-x", and, of course, the Converses of the last four </s>
<s> pg174 _____ _/ ___ \_ / / y \ \ | \___/ | \_ x _/ \_____/ Similarly, with this Diagram, the following Propositions are true:--"All y are x", "No y are not-x", "Some y are x", "Some x are not-y", "Some not-x are not-y", and, of course, the Converses of the last four </s>
<s> _____ _____ _/ \_ _/ \_ / \ / \ | x | | y | \_ _/ \_ _/ \_____/ \_____/ Similarly, with this Diagram, the following are true:--"All x are not-y", "All y are not-x", "No x are y", "Some x are not-y", "Some y are not-x", "Some not-x are not-y", and the Converses of the last four </s>
<s> _____ _____ _/ \_/ \_ / / \ \ | x | | y | \_ \_/ _/ \_____/ \_____/ Similarly, with this Diagram, the following are true:--"Some x are y", "Some x are not-y", "Some not-x are y", "Some not-x are not-y", and of course, their four Converses </s>
<s> Note that _all_ Euler's Diagrams assert "Some not-x are not-y" </s>
<s> Apparently it never occured to him that it might _sometimes_ fail to be true </s>
<s> Now, to represent "All x are y", the _first_ of these Diagrams would suffice </s>
<s> Similarly, to represent "No x are y", the _third_ would suffice </s>
<s> But to represent any _Particular_ Proposition, at least _three_ Diagrams would be needed (in order to include all the possible cases), and, for "Some not-x are not-y", all the _four_ </s>
<s> Â§ 6 </s>
<s> _Venn's Method of Diagrams._ Let us represent "not-x" by "x'" </s>
<s> Mr Venn's Method of Diagrams is a great advance on the above Method </s>
<s> He uses the last of the above Diagrams to represent _any_ desired relation between x and y, by simply shading a Compartment known to be _empty_, and placing a + in one known to be _occupied_ </s>
<s> Thus, he would represent the three Propositions "Some x are y", "No x are y", and "All x are y", as follows:-- _____ _____ _/ \_/ \_ / / \ \ | | + | | \_ \_/ _/ \_____/ \_____/ _____ _____ _/ \_/ \_ / /#\ \ | |###| | \_ \#/ _/ \_____/ \_____/ _____ _____ _/#####\_/ \_ /#######/ \ \ |#######| + | | \#######\_/ _/ \#####/ \_____/ pg175 It will be seen that, of the _four_ Classes, whose peculiar Sets of Attributes are xy, xy', x'y, and x'y', only _three_ are here provided with closed Compartments, while the _fourth_ is allowed the rest of the Infinite Plane to range about in </s>
<s> This arrangement would involve us in very serious trouble, if we ever attempted to represent "No x' are y'" </s>
<s> Mr Venn _once_ (at p </s>
<s> 281) encounters this awful task; but evades it, in a quite masterly fashion, by the simple foot-note "We have not troubled to shade the outside of this diagram" </s>
<s> To represent _two_ Propositions (containing a common Term) _together_, a _three_-letter Diagram is needed </s>
<s> This is the one used by Mr Venn </s>
<s> _____ _/ \_ _/___ x ___\_ _/| \_/ |\_ / \_ / \ _/ \ | \|___|/ | \_ m \_/ y _/ \_____/ \_____/ Here, again, we have only _seven_ closed Compartments, to accommodate the _eight_ Classes whose peculiar Sets of Attributes are xym, xym', &c </s>
<s> "With four terms in request," Mr Venn says, "the most simple and symmetrical diagram seems to me that produced by making four ellipses intersect one another in the desired manner" </s>
<s> This, however, provides only _fifteen_ closed compartments </s>
<s> b ____ ____ c / \ / \ a ___/___ \/ ___\___ d / \ \ /\ / / \ / \ \/ \/ / \ \ \ /\ /\ / / \ \/ \/ \/ / \ /\ /\ /\ / \ \ \/ \/ / / \ \/\ /\/ / \ /\_\/_/\ / \__\______/__/ For _five_ letters, "the simplest diagram I can suggest," Mr Venn says, "is one like this (the small ellipse in the centre is to be regarded as a portion of the _outside_ of c; i.e </s>
<s> its four component portions are inside b and d but are no part of c) </s>
<s> It must be admitted that such a diagram is not quite so simple to draw as one might wish it to be; but then consider what the alternative is of one undertakes to deal with five terms and all their combinations--nothing short of the disagreeable task of writing out, or in some way putting before us, all the 32 combinations involved" </s>
<s> b c d ______ ____ ______ ______/_ \/ \/ _\______ a / / \ /\ /\ / \ \ e / / \ / \ / \ / \ \ / \ \/ \/ \/ / \ / \ /\ /\ /\ / \ / \ / \ / \ / \ / \ | \/ \/ __ \/ \/ | | /\ /\/ \/\ /\ | | / \ / /\ /\ \ / \ | | | \/ | \/ | \/ | | | | /\ | /\ | /\ | | | \ / \ \/ \/ / \ / | \ \/ \/\__/\/ \/ / \ /\ /\ /\ /\ / \ / \ / \ / \ / \ / \ / \/ \/ \/ \ / \ \ /\ /\ /\ / / \ \ / \ / \ / \ / / \ \/ \/ \/ \/ / \ /\____/\____/\____/\ / \ / \ / \| |/ \____________________/ pg176 This Diagram gives us 31 closed compartments </s>
<s> For _six_ letters, Mr Venn suggests that we might use _two_ Diagrams, like the above, one for the f-part, and the other for the not-f-part, of all the other combinations </s>
<s> "This", he says, "would give the desired 64 subdivisions" </s>
<s> This, however, would only give 62 closed Compartments, and _one_ infinite area, which the two Classes, a'b'c'd'e'f and a'b'c'd'e'f', would have to share between them </s>
<s> Beyond _six_ letters Mr Venn does not go </s>
<s> Â§ 7 </s>
<s> _My Method of Diagrams._ My Method of Diagrams _resembles_ Mr Venn's, in having separate Compartments assigned to the various Classes, and in marking these Compartments as _occupied_ or as _empty_; but it _differs_ from his Method, in assigning a _closed_ area to the _Universe of Discourse_, so that the Class which, under Mr Venn's liberal sway, has been ranging at will through Infinite Space, is suddenly dismayed to find itself "cabin'd, cribb'd, confined", in a limited Cell like any other Class </s>
<s> Also I use _rectilinear_, instead of _curvilinear_, Figures; and I mark an _occupied_ Cell with a 'I' (meaning that there is at least _one_ Thing in it), and an _empty_ Cell with a 'O' (meaning that there is _no_ Thing in it) </s>
<s> For _two_ letters, I use this Diagram, in which the North Half is assigned to 'x', the South to 'not-x' (or 'x''), the West to y, and the East to y' </s>
<s> Thus the N.W </s>
<s> Cell contains the xy-Class, the N.E </s>
<s> Cell the xy'-Class, and so on </s>
<s> Â·-------Â· | | | |---|---| | | | Â·-------Â· For _three_ letters, I subdivide these four Cells, by drawing an _Inner_ Square, which I assign to m, the _Outer_ Border being assigned to m' </s>
<s> I thus get _eight_ Cells that are needed to accommodate the eight Classes, whose peculiar Sets of Attributes are xym, xym', &c </s>
<s> Â·---------------Â· | | | | Â·---|---Â· | | | | | | |---|---|---|---| | | | | | | Â·---|---Â· | | | | Â·---------------Â· This last Diagram is the most complex that I use in the _Elementary_ Part of my 'Symbolic Logic' </s>
<s> But I may as well take this opportunity of describing the more complex ones which will appear in Part II </s>
<s> pg177 For _four_ letters (which I call a, b, c, d) I use this Diagram; assigning the North Half to a (and of course the _rest_ of the Diagram to a'), the West Half to b, the Horizontal Oblong to c, and the Upright Oblong to d </s>
<s> We have now got 16 Cells </s>
<s> Â·---------------------Â· | | | | Â·---|---Â· | | | | | | | Â·---|---|---|---Â· | | | | | | | | |--|---|---|---|---|--| | | | | | | | | Â·---|---|---|---Â· | | | | | | | Â·---|---Â· | | | | Â·---------------------Â· For _five_ letters (adding e) I subdivide the 16 Cells of the previous Diagram by _oblique_ partitions, assigning all the _upper_ portions to e, and all the _lower_ portions to e' </s>
<s> Here, I admit, we lose the advantage of having the e-Class all _together_, "in a ring-fence", like the other 4 Classes </s>
<s> Still, it is very easy to find; and the operation, of erasing it, is nearly as easy as that of erasing any other Class </s>
<s> We have now got 32 Cells </s>
<s> Â·---------------------Â· | / | / | | / Â·---|---Â· / | | / | / | / | / | | Â·---|---|---|---Â· | | | / | / | / | / | | |--|---|---|---|---|--| | | / | / | / | / | | | Â·---|---|---|---Â· | | / | / | / | / | | / Â·---|---Â· / | | / | / | Â·---------------------Â· For _six_ letters (adding h, as I avoid _tailed_ letters) I substitute upright crosses for the oblique partitions, assigning the 4 portions, into which each of the 16 Cells is thus divided, to the four Classes eh, eh', e'h, e'h' </s>
<s> We have now got 64 Cells </s>

<s> Â§ 8 </s>
<s> _Solution of a Syllogism by various Methods._ The best way, I think, to exhibit the differences between these various Methods of solving Syllogisms, will be to take a concrete example, and solve it by each Method in turn </s>
<s> Let us take, as our example, No </s>
<s> 29 (see p </s>
<s> 102) </s>
<s> "No philosophers are conceited; Some conceited persons are not gamblers </s>
<s> '. </s>
<s> Some persons, who are not gamblers, are not philosophers" </s>
<s> pg180 (1) _Solution by ordinary Method._ These Premisses, as they stand, will give no Conclusion, as they are both negative </s>
<s> If by 'Permutation' or 'Obversion', we write the Minor Premiss thus, 'Some conceited persons are not-gamblers,' we can get a Conclusion in _Fresison_, viz </s>
<s> "No philosophers are conceited; Some conceited persons are not-gamblers </s>
<s> '. </s>
<s> Some not-gamblers are not philosophers" This can be proved by reduction to _Ferio_, thus:-- "No conceited persons are philosophers; Some not-gamblers are conceited </s>
<s> '. </s>
<s> Some not-gamblers are not philosophers" </s>
<s> The validity of _Ferio_ follows directly from the Axiom '_De Omni et Nullo_' </s>
<s> (2) _Symbolic Representation._ Before proceeding to discuss other Methods of Solution, it is necessary to translate our Syllogism into an _abstract_ form </s>
<s> Let us take "persons" as our 'Universe of Discourse'; and let xÂ =Â "philosophers", mÂ =Â "conceited", and yÂ =Â "gamblers" </s>
<s> Then the Syllogism may be written thus:-- "No x are m; Some m are y' </s>
<s> '. </s>
<s> Some y' are x'" </s>
<s> (3) _Solution by Euler's Method of Diagrams._ The Major Premiss requires only _one_ Diagram, viz </s>
<s> 1 _____ _____ _/ \_ _/ \_ / \ / \ | x | | m | \_ _/ \_ _/ \_____/ \_____/ pg181 The Minor requires _three_, viz </s>

<s> (4) _Solution by Venn's Method of Diagrams._ The following Solution has been kindly supplied to me Mr Venn himself </s>
<s> "The Minor Premiss declares that some of the constituents in my' must be saved: mark these constituents with a cross </s>
<s> _____ _/ + \_ _/___ ___\_ _/|##+#\_/ |\_ / \###/#\ _/ \ | + \|_#_|/ | \_ m \_/ y _/ \_____/ \_____/ The Major declares that all xm must be destroyed; erase it </s>

<s> That is, there must exist my'x'; or eliminating m, y'x' </s>
<s> In common phraseology, 'Some y' are x',' or, 'Some not-gamblers are not-philosophers'." pg183 (5) _Solution by my Method of Diagrams._ The first Premiss asserts that no xm exist: so we mark the xm-Compartment as empty, by placing a 'O' in each of its Cells </s>
<s> The second asserts that some my' exist: so we mark the my'-Compartment as occupied, by placing a 'I' in its only available Cell </s>

<s> that some x'y' exist </s>
<s> Hence "Some x' are y'": i.e </s>

<s> Â§ 9 </s>
<s> _My Method of treating Syllogisms and Sorites._ Of all the strange things, that are to be met with in the ordinary text-books of Formal Logic, perhaps the strangest is the violent contrast one finds to exist between their ways of dealing with these two subjects </s>
<s> While they have elaborately discussed no less than _nineteen_ different forms of _Syllogisms_----each with its own special and exasperating Rules, while the whole constitute an almost useless machine, for practical purposes, many of the Conclusions being incomplete, and many quite legitimate forms being ignored----they have limited _Sorites_ to _two_ forms only, of childish simplicity; and these they have dignified with special _names_, apparently under the impression that no other possible forms existed </s>
<s> As to _Syllogisms_, I find that their nineteen forms, with about a score of others which they have ignored, can all be arranged under _three_ forms, each with a very simple Rule of its own; and the only question the Reader has to settle, in working any one of the 101 Examples given at p </s>
<s> 101 of this book, is "Does it belong to Fig </s>
<s> I., II., or III." </s>
<s> pg184 As to _Sorites_, the only two forms, recognised by the text-books, are the _Aristotelian_, whose Premisses are a series of Propositions in A, so arranged that the Predicate of each is the Subject of the next, and the _Goclenian_, whose Premisses are the very same series, written backwards </s>
<s> Goclenius, it seems, was the first who noticed the startling fact that it does not affect the force of a Syllogism to invert the order of its Premisses, and who applied this discovery to a Sorites </s>
<s> If we assume (as surely we may?) that he is the _same_ man as that transcendent genius who first noticed that 4 times 5 is the same thing as 5 times 4, we may apply to him what somebody (Edmund Yates, I think it was) has said of Tupper, viz., "here is a man who, beyond all others of his generation, has been favoured with Glimpses of the Obvious" </s>
<s> These puerile----not to say infantine----forms of a Sorites I have, in this book, ignored from the very first, and have not only admitted freely Propositions in _E_, but have purposely stated the Premisses in random order, leaving to the Reader the useful task of arranging them, for himself, in an order which can be worked as a series of regular Syllogisms </s>
<s> In doing this, he can begin with _any one_ of them he likes </s>
<s> I have tabulated, for curiosity, the various orders in which the Premisses of the Aristotelian Sorites 1 </s>
<s> All a are b; 2 </s>
<s> All b are c; 3 </s>
<s> All c are d; 4 </s>
<s> All d are e; 5 </s>
<s> All e are h </s>
<s> '. </s>
<s> All a are h </s>
<s> may be syllogistically arranged, and I find there are no less than _sixteen_ such orders, viz., 12345, 21345, 23145, 23415, 23451, 32145, 32415, 32451, 34215, 34251, 34521, 43215, 43251, 43521, 45321, 54321 </s>
<s> Of these the _first_ and the _last_ have been dignified with names; but the other _fourteen_----first enumerated by an obscure Writer on Logic, towards the end of the Nineteenth Century----remain without a name </s>
<s> pg185 Â§ 10 </s>
<s> _Some account of Parts II, III._ In Part II </s>
<s> will be found some of the matters mentioned in this Appendix, viz., the "Existential Import" of Propositions, the use of a _negative_ Copula, and the theory that "two negative Premisses prove nothing" </s>
<s> I shall also extend the range of Syllogisms, by introducing Propositions containing alternatives (such as "Not-all x are y"), Propositions containing 3 or more Terms (such as "All ab are c", which, taken along with "Some bc' are d", would prove "Some d are a'"), &c </s>
<s> I shall also discuss Sorites containing Entities, and the _very_ puzzling subjects of Hypotheticals and Dilemmas </s>
<s> I hope, in the course of Part II., to go over all the ground usually traversed in the text-books used in our Schools and Universities, and to enable my Readers to solve Problems of the same kind as, and far harder than, those that are at present set in their Examinations </s>
<s> In Part III </s>
<s> I hope to deal with many curious and out-of-the-way subjects, some of which are not even alluded to in any of the treatises I have met with </s>
<s> In this Part will be found such matters as the Analysis of Propositions into their Elements (let the Reader, who has never gone into this branch of the subject, try to make out for himself what _additional_ Proposition would be needed to convert "Some a are b" into "Some a are bc"), the treatment of Numerical and Geometrical Problems, the construction of Problems, and the solution of Syllogisms and Sorites containing Propositions more complex than any that I have used in Part II </s>
<s> I will conclude with eight Problems, as a taste of what is coming in Part II </s>
<s> I shall be very glad to receive, from any Reader, who thinks he has solved any one of them (more especially if he has done so _without_ using any Method of Symbols), what he conceives to be its complete Conclusion </s>
<s> It may be well to explain what I mean by the _complete_ Conclusion of a Syllogism or a Sorites </s>
<s> I distinguish their Terms as being of two kinds----those which _can_ be eliminated (e.g </s>
<s> the Middle Term of a Syllogism), which I call the "Eliminands," and those which _cannot_, which I call the "Retinends"; and I do not call the Conclusion _complete_, unless it states _all_ the relations among the Retinends only, which can be deduced from the Premisses </s>

<s> One of the Monitors (who is a great reader of Wilkie Collins' novels) is very observant, and takes MS </s>

<s> breaks off suddenly </s>

<s> [N.B </s>
<s> In this Problem, it is assumed that the phrase "if Barry takes salt" allows of _two_ possible cases, viz </s>
<s> (1) "he takes salt _only_"; (2) "he takes _both_ condiments" </s>
<s> And so with all similar phrases </s>
<s> It is also assumed that the phrase "either Cole or Lang takes _one_ only of the two condiments" allows _three_ possible cases, viz </s>
<s> (1) "Cole takes _one_ only, Lang takes both or neither"; (2) "Cole takes both or neither, Lang takes _one_ only"; (3) "Cole takes _one_ only, Lang takes _one_ only" </s>
<s> And so with all similar phrases </s>
<s> It is also assumed that every rule is to be understood as implying the words "and _vice versÃ¢_" </s>
<s> Thus the first rule would imply the addition "and, if either Cole or Lang takes only _one_ condiment, then Barry takes salt".] pg193 7 </s>
